Commonwealth v. Arter


No. 63 MAP 2015


SUPREME COURT OF PENNSYLVANIA


151 A.3d 149; 2016 Pa. LEXIS 2916


April 5, 2016, Argued 
December 28, 2016, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal from the Order of the Superior Court dated October 8, 2014 at No. 396 MDA 2014 dated October 8, 2014, reconsideration denied December 2, 2014, Affirming the Judgment of Sentence of Dauphin County Court of Common Pleas, Criminal Division, at No. CP-22-CR-0001297-2012, dated February 4, 2014. Appeal allowed July 28, 2015 at 11 MAL 2015. Trial Copurt Judge: Chris R. Wogan, Intermediate Court Judges: Jack A. Panella, Judge, Anne E. Lazarus, Judge, Patricia H. Jenkins, Judge.
Commonwealth v. Arter, 108 A.3d 108, 2014 Pa. Super. Unpub. LEXIS 2312 (2014)


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: HOLDINGS: [1]-The order affirming the trial court's denial of appellant's motion to suppress was reversed because the illegally-obtained evidence, which should have been suppressed during the criminal proceedings, should likewise have been suppressed during appellant's parole and probation revocation proceedings pursuant to Pa. Const. art. I, § 8; [2]-The Court held that the exclusion rule applies to parole and probation revocation proceedings pursuant to Pa. Const. art. I, § 8.


OUTCOME: Order reversed; order revoking appellant's parole vacated; case remanded to trial court for further proceeding.

 

2 of 2746 DOCUMENTS


Commonwealth v. Barnes


No. 36 EAP 2015


SUPREME COURT OF PENNSYLVANIA


151 A.3d 121; 2016 Pa. LEXIS 2910


September 13, 2016, Argued 
December 28, 2016, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal from the judgment of Superior Court entered on 6/27/2014 at No. 1784 EDA 2013 affirming the judgment of sentence entered on 11/1/2010 in the Court of Common Pleas, Philadelphia County, Criminal Division, at No. CP-51-CR-0005943-2009. Appeal allowed September 18, 2015 at 350 EAL 2014. Trial Court Judge: Chris R. Wogan, Judge. Intermediate Court Judges:Jack A. Panella, Judge, Anne E. Lazarus, Judge, Patricia H. Jenkins, Judge.
Commonwealth v. Barnes, 105 A.3d 47, 2014 Pa. Super. LEXIS 2935 (Pa. Super. Ct., 2014)


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: HOLDINGS: [1]-The Court held that when the mandatory minimum sentencing authority on which the sentencing court relied is rendered void on its face, and no separate mandatory authority supported the sentence, any sentence entered under such purported authority is an illegal sentence for issue preservation purposes on direct appeal. Thus, the appellant is entitled to resentencing notwithstanding his failure to preserve his issue prior to seeking the Court's review.


OUTCOME: e reverse the Superior Court's decision, vacate Appellant's judgment of sentence, and remand for resentencing.

4 of 2746 DOCUMENTS


Commonwealth v. Knight


No. 702 CAP


SUPREME COURT OF PENNSYLVANIA


156 A.3d 239; 2016 Pa. LEXIS 2659


October 7, 2015, Submitted 
November 22, 2016, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal from the Judgment of Sentence entered on August 31, 2014 in the Court of Common Pleas, Westmoreland County, Criminal Division at No. CP-65-CR-0000851-2010. Post Sentence Motions Denied July 16, 2014.
Commonwealth v. Smyrnes, 2012 Pa. LEXIS 1381 (Pa., June 20, 2012)


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: HOLDINGS: [1]-Appellant's capital murder judgment of sentence was vacated and he was awarded a new penalty hearing because the jury's weighing deliberation did not include a second mitigator of no prior criminal history it was required to find, which introduced an arbitrary factor; [2]-The Court found sufficient evidence supported appellant's first-degree murder conviction based on the nature of the injuries inflicted upon vital parts of the victim's body, appellant's active role in inflicting many of those injuries, his plea admitting to the crime, and his intent to kill was amply demonstrated by his stabbing the victim in the chest multiple times with a knife, and then slashing her neck.


OUTCOME: Judgment of sentence vacated; case remanded to trial court for a new penalty hearing.

Commonwealth v. Veon


No. 69 MAP 2015, No. 70 MAP 2015


SUPREME COURT OF PENNSYLVANIA


150 A.3d 435; 2016 Pa. LEXIS 2613


May 10, 2016, Argued 
November 22, 2016, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal from the Order of the Superior Court at No. 1698 MDA 2012 dated February 6, 2015 Affirming, Vacating & Remanding the Judgment of Sentence of the Dauphin County Court of Common Pleas, Criminal Division, at No. CP-22-CR-0004274-2009 dated November 8, 2012. Appeal allowed August 20, 2015 at 192 MAL 2015. Trial Court Judge: Bruce F Bratton, Judge. Intermediate Ct. Judges: Jack A Panella, Judge, Sallie Mundy, Judge, William Platt, Judge.

Appeal from the Order of the Superior Court at No. 2168 MDA 2012 dated February 6, 2015 Quashing the Order of the Dauphin County Court of Common Pleas, Criminal Division, at No. CP-22-CR-0004274-2009 dated November 8, 2012.
Commonwealth v. Veon, 2015 PA Super 26, 109 A.3d 754, 2015 Pa. Super. LEXIS 36 (Pa. Super. Ct., 2015)


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: HOLDINGS: [1]-Appellant's judgment of sentence for violating the criminal conflict of interest statute, 65 Pa.C.S. § 1103(a), was reversed because based upon the plain language of 65 Pa.C.S. § 1102, to prove pecuniary benefit as used in the statute, the prosecution must show some private financial gain and, consequently, the trial court erred when it instructed the jury that § 1102 could be violated when the only benefit to appellant was political in nature; [2]-The court further reversed the judgment of sentence ordering appellant to pay restitution to the Pennsylvania Department of Community Economic Development (DCED) following his conviction for violating the criminal conflict of interest statute, 65 Pa.C.S. § 1103(a), was reversed because the DCED was neither a direct victim nor a reimbursable compensating government agency under 65 Pa.C.S. § 1106.


OUTCOME: Judgment of sentence vacated; case remanded to trial court for a new trial.

Pa. State Educ. Ass'n v. Commonwealth


No. 11 MAP 2015, No. 22 MAP 2015


SUPREME COURT OF PENNSYLVANIA


148 A.3d 142; 2016 Pa. LEXIS 2337; 41 I.E.R. Cas. (BNA) 1310


April 5, 2016, Argued 
October 18, 2016, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal from the Order of the Commonwealth Court at No. 396 MD 2009 dated February 17, 2015. Renee Cohn Jubelirer, Judge, Dan Pellegrini, President Judge, Bonnie Brigance Leadbetter, Judge, Bernard L. McGinley, Judge, Kevin P. Brobson, Judge, Patricia A. McCullough, Judge, Anne E. Covey, Judge.
Pa. State Educ. Ass'n v. Commonwealth, 110 A.3d 1076, 2015 Pa. Commw. LEXIS 72 (Pa. Commw. Ct., 2015)


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: HOLDINGS: [1]-The Court held that the right to informational privacy is guaranteed by Pa. Const. art. I, § 1 and may not be violated unless outweighed by a public interest favoring disclosure; [2]-As such, the Court held that the lower appellate court erred in ruling that there is no constitutional right to privacy in one's home address in connection with Right to Know Law (RTKL), 65 Pa. Stat. Ann. §§ 67.101-67.3104, requests as the right to informational privacy is guaranteed by Pa. Const. art. I, § 8, and the balancing weighed in favor of the public school employees on the facts and circumstances presented in the case.


OUTCOME: Judgment reversed.

Commonwealth v. Ball


No. 23 MAP 2015


SUPREME COURT OF PENNSYLVANIA


146 A.3d 755; 2016 Pa. LEXIS 2179


November 17, 2015, Argued; May 10, 2016, Reargued 
September 28, 2016, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal from the Order of the Superior Court dated July 24, 2014, Reconsideration Denied September 3, 2014, at No. 2086 MDA 2013, Reversing the Judgment of Sentence of the Cumberland County Court of Common Pleas, Criminal Division, dated October 22, 2013, at No. CP-21-SA-0000133-2013. Appeal allowed March 24, 2015 at 719 MAL 2014. Trial Court Judge: Albert H. Masland, Judge. Intermediate Court Judges: Anne E. Lazarus, Judge, Victor P. Stabile, Judge, John L. Musmanno, Judge.
Commonwealth v. Ball, 2014 PA Super 160, 97 A.3d 397, 2014 Pa. Super. LEXIS 2312 (Pa. Super. Ct., 2014)


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: HOLDINGS: [1]-The Court agreed that defendant's double jeopardy right was violated when the Commonwealth tried him twice for driving while his operating privileges were suspended and while intoxicated as his choice in pursuing a trial de novo under Pa. R. Crim. P. 462(A) instead of accepting the Magisterial District Judge's election to convict him of an uncharged, lesser included offense did not waive his double jeopardy rights; [2]-However, the lower appellate court erred by discharging defendant completely since pursuant to Rule 462(A), he was entitled to have that conviction reviewed de novo in the court of common pleas, not a total discharge as to his duly convicted offense.


OUTCOME: Order affirmed, in part; reversed, in part, as to order of discharge; case remanded to trial court for a de novo trial.

Commonwealth v. Martinez


No. 30 MAP 2015, No. 32 MAP 2015, No. 34 MAP 2015


SUPREME COURT OF PENNSYLVANIA


147 A.3d 517; 2016 Pa. LEXIS 2183


March 8, 2016, Argued 
September 28, 2016, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal from the Order of the Superior Court at No. 1420 MDA 2013, dated April 14, 2014, Affirming the Order of the York County Court of Common Pleas, Criminal Division, at No. CP-67-CR-0001486-2010, dated July 19, 2013. Appeal Allowed April 8, 2015 at 328 MAL 2014. Trial Court Judge: Michael E. Borner, Judge. Intermediate Court Judges: Jack A. Panella, Christine Donohue, Sallie Mundy, JJ.

Appeal from the Order of the Superior Court at No. 1522 MDA 2013 dated April 14, 2014 Affirming the Order of the York County Court of Common Pleas, Criminal Division, at No. CP-67-CR-0000227-2011, dated July 31, 2013. Appeal Allowed April 8, 2015 at 330 MAL 2014. Trial Court Judge: Michael E. Bortner, Judge. Intermediate Court Judges: Jack A. Panella, Christine Donohue, Sallie Mundy, JJ.

Appeal from the Order of the Superior Court at No. 1422 MDA 2013 dated April 15, 2014 Affirming the Order of the York County Court of Common Pleas, Criminal Division, at No.CP-67-CR-0006313-2005, dated July 19, 2013. Appeal Allowed April 8, 2015 at 339 MAL 2014. Trial Court Judge: Stephen P. Linebaugh, President Judge. Intermediate Court Judges: Jack A. Pnaella, Christine Donohue, Sallie Mundy, JJ.
Commonwealth v. Grace, 102 A.3d 531, 2014 Pa. Super. LEXIS 2134 (Pa. Super. Ct., 2014)
Commonwealth v. Shower, 102 A.3d 533, 2014 Pa. Super. LEXIS 2051 (Pa. Super. Ct., 2014)
Commonwealth v. Martinez, 102 A.3d 530, 2014 Pa. Super. LEXIS 2092 (Pa. Super. Ct., 2014)


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: HOLDINGS: [1]-In three consolidated appeals, the Court held that appellees were entitled to the benefit of the bargains struck with the Commonwealth when the trial court accepted their plea agreements and affirmed that their sexual offender registration requirements were governed by Megan's Law, 42 Pa.C.S. §§ 9791-9799.9 (expired), which was in effect when appellees entered their plea agreements, and not by the Sex Offender Registration and Notification Act, 42 Pa.C.S. §§ 9799.10-9799.41, which superseded Megan's Law; [2]-As a result, one appellee was not required to register as a sexual offender pursuant to the plea agreement he entered into with the Commonwealth, and the other two appellees were subject to certain terms of registration as a sex offender, as opposed to lifetime registration.


OUTCOME: Orders affirmed.

Robinson Twp. v. Commonwealth


No. 104 MAP 2014; No. 105 MAP 2014


SUPREME COURT OF PENNSYLVANIA


147 A.3d 536; 2016 Pa. LEXIS 2190; 46 ELR 20156


March 9, 2016, Argued 
September 28, 2016, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal from the Order of the Commonwealth Court at Docket No. 284 MD 2012, dated July 17, 2014. Other Court Judges: Patricia A. McCullough, Dan Pellegrini, President Judge, Bonnie Brigance, Leadbetter, Robert E. Simpson, P. Kevin Brobson, JJ.

Appeal from the Order of the Commonwealth Court at Docket No. 284 MD 2012, dated July 17, 2014. Other Court Judges: Patricia A. McCullough, Dan Pellegrini, President Judge, Bonnie Brigance Leadbetter, Robert E. Simpson, P. Kevin Brobson, JJ.
Robinson Twp. v. Commonwealth, 96 A.3d 1104, 2014 Pa. Commw. LEXIS 367 (Pa. Commw. Ct., 2014)


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: HOLDINGS: [1]-58 Pa.C.S. §§ 3305-3509 were not severable from the now-enjoined 58 Pa.C.S. §§ 3303 and 3304, so those sections were also enjoined; [2]-Act 13 did not violate Pa. Const. art. III, § 3, the single subject rule; [3]-58 Pa.C.S. §§ 3218.1, 3222.1(b)(10), (11) contravened Pa. Const. art. III, § 32 of the Pennsylvania Constitution, because they constituted special legislation, so those sections were stricken and enjoined from further application and enforcement; [4]-The court stayed its mandate with respect to § 3218.1 so the General Assembly could enact remedial legislation; [5]-58 Pa.C.S. § 3241 was unconstitutional on its face as it granted a corporation the power of eminent domain to take private property for a private purpose, in violation of the Fifth Amendment and Pa. Const. art. I, § 10, so it was stricken and enjoined from further application and enforcement.


OUTCOME: Judgment affirmed in part and reversed in part.

Taylor v. Extendicare Health Facilities, Inc.


No. 19 WAP 2015


SUPREME COURT OF PENNSYLVANIA


147 A.3d 490; 2016 Pa. LEXIS 2166


April 5, 2016, Argued 
September 28, 2016, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: US Supreme Court certiorari denied by Taylor v. Extendicare Health Facilities, Inc., 2017 U.S. LEXIS 2106 (U.S., Mar. 27, 2017)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal from the Order of the Superior Court entered April 2, 2015 at No. 2028 WDA 2013, affirming the Order of the Court of Common Pleas of Washington County entered November 20, 2013 at No. 2012-6878. Appeal Allowed September 23, 2015 at 161 WAL 2015. Trial Court Judge: Debbie O'Dell Seneca, President Judge. Intermediate Court Judges: John T. Bender, President Judge Emeritus, Mary Jane Bowes, Cheryl Lynn Allen, JJ.
Taylor v. Extendicare Health Facilities, Inc., 2015 PA Super 64, 113 A.3d 317, 2015 Pa. Super. LEXIS 144 (Pa. Super. Ct., Apr. 2, 2015)


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: ISSUE: Whether the Federal Arbitration Act (FAA), 9 U.S.C.S. §§ 1 - 14, preempted a lower courts' application of Pa.R.C.P. No. 213(e), which required the consolidation of survival and wrongful death actions for trial, when a representative of a nursing center executed an arbitration agreement with the decedent requiring the arbitration of claims arising from the decedent's stay at the nursing center facility and the coexecutors of the decedent's estate brought wrongful death claims on behalf of themselves as wrongful death beneficiaries and survival claims on behalf of the decedent's estate. HOLDINGS: [1]-The FAA preempted the application of Rule 213(e), which was a procedural mechanism to control case flow and conflicted with the FAA, and required arbitration of the survival claim against the nursing center.


OUTCOME: Judgment reversed, and case remanded for further proceedings.

Mount Airy #1, LLC v. Pa. Dep't of Revenue


No. 34 EM 2015


SUPREME COURT OF PENNSYLVANIA


154 A.3d 268; 2016 Pa. LEXIS 2174


March 8, 2016, Argued 
September 28, 2016, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Related proceeding at In re Amendment to the Pa. Race Horse Dev. & Gaming Act, 164 A.3d 492, 2017 Pa. LEXIS 154 (Pa., Jan. 20, 2017)
Related proceeding at Mount Airy # 1, LLC v. Pa. Dep't of Revenue, 2017 Pa. LEXIS 2058 (Pa., Sept. 1, 2017)
Related proceeding at Chester Downs & Marina LLC v. Pa. Dep't of Revenue, 2017 Pa. LEXIS 2718 (Pa., Oct. 31, 2017)


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: HOLDINGS: [1]-In a suit brought by a casino challenging the constitutionality of the Pennsylvania Race Horse Development and Gaming Act (Gaming Act), 4 Pa.C.S. § 1403(c), the Court held that the local share assessment set forth in the Pennsylvania Race Horse Development and Gaming Act, 4 Pa.C.S. § 1403(c)(2) and (c)(3), was a non-uniform tax prohibited by the Uniformity Clause, Pa. Const. art. VIII, § 1, and struck those two subsections from the Gaming Act.


OUTCOME: Casino awarded declaratory relief; decision stayed for 120 days.

 

13 of 2746 DOCUMENTS


D.P. v. G.J.P.


No. 25 WAP 2015


SUPREME COURT OF PENNSYLVANIA


146 A.3d 204; 2016 Pa. LEXIS 2003


April 5, 2016, Argued 
September 9, 2016, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal from the Order of the Court of Common Pleas of Westmoreland County dated September 8, 2015 at No. 1750 of 2014-D.
Ponko v. Ponko, 2015 Pa. Dist. & Cnty. Dec. LEXIS 191 (2015)


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: HOLDINGS: [1]-In grandparents' (GPs) action for partial physical custody of the minor grandchildren, 23 Pa.C.S. § 5325(2), which granted the GPs standing to seek custody based on the parents' separation for at least six months, required review under strict scrutiny for purposes of claims regarding due process and equal protection under U.S. Const. amend. XIV, § 1; [2]-Section 5325(2) did not withstand strict scrutiny, such that it violated parents' fundamental rights under due process, as it was not narrowly tailored to a compelling governmental interest; [3]-However, as § 5325(2) was severable from the remainder of § 5325 involving standing for GPs who sought custody and visitation in other circumstances, the one portion of the provision that was deemed unconstitutional was severed from the remainder of the statute.


OUTCOME: Order dismissing complaint affirmed.

Herder Spring Hunting Club v. Keller


No. 5 MAP 2015


SUPREME COURT OF PENNSYLVANIA


143 A.3d 358; 2016 Pa. LEXIS 1512


October 7, 2015, Argued; January 20, 2016, Submitted 
July 19, 2016, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: US Supreme Court certiorari denied by Keller v. Herder Spring Hunting Club, 2017 U.S. LEXIS 647 (U.S., Jan. 9, 2017)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal from the Order of the Superior Court at No. 718 MDA 2013 dated May 9, 2014, reconsideration denied July 11, 2014, vacating the Judgment of the Centre County Court of Common Pleas, Civil Division, entered on July 12, 2011 at No. 2008-3434 and remanding. Trial Court Judge: Bradley P. Lunsford, Judge. Intermediate Court Judges: Christine Donohue, Judge, Paula Francisco Ott, Judge, William Platt, Judge.
Herder Spring Hunting Club v. Keller, 2014 PA Super 100, 93 A.3d 465, 2014 Pa. Super. LEXIS 699 (Pa. Super. Ct., 2014)


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: HOLDINGS: [1]-In a quiet title action concerning the ownership of subsurface rights to an unseated tract of land, the Court affirmed the order vacating the grant of summary judgment in favor of appellants, who bought the property at a tax sale in 1894 and sold the surface rights to others, reserving the subsurface rights to themselves, because the Court found that a 1935 tax sale resulted in the transfer of the entire property, including both the surface and subsurface estates, thus, appellee, who had subsequently purchased the property, was entitled to summary judgment; [2]-The Court held that the tax sale extinguished all previous titles and in the absence of a separate assessment of the minerals, such as in the case at bar, the entire property was subject to the tax sale.


OUTCOME: Order affirmed; case remanded to trial court for further proceedings.

 

16 of 2746 DOCUMENTS


Commonwealth v. Washington


No. 37 EAP 2015


SUPREME COURT OF PENNSYLVANIA


142 A.3d 810; 2016 Pa. LEXIS 1536


April 7, 2016, Submitted 
July 19, 2016, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal from the Judgment of Superior Court entered on 5/12/15 at No. 532 EDA 2011 reversing the order entered on 8/6/08 in the Court of Common Pleas, Philadelphia County, Criminal Division, at Nos. CP-51-0711021, 0711141, and 1009712-1996 and CP-51-CR-1107481, 1107621, 1107651 and 1107671-1997. Trial Court Judge: Genece E. Brinkley, Judge. Intermediate Court Judges: John L. Musmanno, Judge; Mary Jane Bowes, Judge; Jack A. Panella, Judge.
Commonwealth v. Washington, 122 A.3d 446, 2015 Pa. Super. Unpub. LEXIS 1345 (2015)


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: ISSUE: Whether the decision of the United States Supreme Court that any fact increasing the penalty for a crime had to be treated as an element of the offense, submitted to a jury, rather than a judge, and found beyond a reasonable doubt applied retroactively to attacks upon mandatory minimum sentences advanced on collateral review. HOLDINGS: [1]-The rule did not apply retroactively to cases pending on collateral review, and thus, defendant's judgment of sentence under 42 Pa.C.S. § 9712(b), was not illegal; [2]-The rule neither altered the range of conduct or the class of persons punished by the law but allocated the relevant decision-making authority to a jury rather than a judge while establishing the beyond-a-reasonable-doubt [3]-It remained for judges to increase sentences in the discretionary sentencing regime based on facts they found by a preponderance of the evidence.


OUTCOME: Order affirmed.

 

17 of 2746 DOCUMENTS


Leach v. Commonwealth


No. 61 MAP 2015


SUPREME COURT OF PENNSYLVANIA


141 A.3d 426; 2016 Pa. LEXIS 1283


March 9, 2016, Argued 
June 20, 2016, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal from the Order of the Commonwealth Court at No. 585 MD 2014 dated 6/25/15. Other Court Judges: Dan Pellegrini, President Judge; Bernard L. McGinley, Judge; Bonnie Brigance, Leadbetter, Judge; Robert E. Simpson, Judge; Mary Hannah Leavitt, Judge; Patricia A. McCullough, Judge; Anne E. Covey, Judge.
Leach v. Commonwealth, 118 A.3d 1271, 2015 Pa. Commw. LEXIS 272 (Pa. Commw. Ct., 2015)


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: HOLDINGS: [1]-The commonwealth court properly granted a request by two cities and several legislators for summary relief, dismissed the legislative leaders' demurrer as moot, and declared Act 192 unconstitutional because Act 192 did not satisfy Pa. Const. art. III, § 3's mandate that each bill contain but one subject where the primary subjects covered by Act 192--including, on the one hand, criminal penalties for theft of copper and aluminum and, on the other hand, the creation of a civil cause of action to challenge municipal firearms legislation--were so disparate as to lack any clear, common nexus, and creating a civil cause of action for persons affected by local gun regulations was simply too far afield from the definition of new offenses relating to the theft of secondary metal to be considered part of one subject.


OUTCOME: Order affirmed.

 

18 of 2746 DOCUMENTS


Commonwealth v. Wolfe


No. 68 MAP 2015


SUPREME COURT OF PENNSYLVANIA


140 A.3d 651; 2016 Pa. LEXIS 1282


November 18, 2015, Argued; January 20, 2016, Resubmitted 
June 20, 2016, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal from the Order of the Superior Court at No. 1962 MDA 2013 dated 12/24/14 vacating and remanding the judgment of sentence of the Lancaster County Court of Common Pleas, Criminal Division, at No. CP-36-CR-5791-2012 dated 10/1/13. Trial Court Judge: Joseph C. Madenspacher, Judge. Intermediate Court Judges: Mary Jane Bowes, Judge; Sallie Mundy, Judge; Patricia H. Jenkins, Judge.
Commonwealth v. Wolfe, 2014 PA Super 288, 106 A.3d 800, 2014 Pa. Super. LEXIS 4977 (Pa. Super. Ct., 2014)


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: HOLDINGS: [1]-42 Pa.C.S. § 9718, requiring imposing a mandatory minimum sentence for a violation of 18 Pa.C.S. § 3123(a)(7) pursuant to judicial fact-finding of facts that were purportedly not crime elements, was properly found, sua sponte, facially unconstitutional because 42 Pa.C.S. § 9718(c) required such fact-finding and was integral to the statute, so 42 Pa.C.S. § 9718(a) did not stand alone, 42 Pa.C.S. § 9718 created a distinct aggravated crime, the statute's judicial fact-finding directive attached to that crime despite a jury verdict, and sentencing judges could not disregard such explicit legislative mandates, so, while a jury found the victim was under 16, the sentencing court had to make its own finding at sentencing but could not do so consistently with U.S. Const. amend. VI, and applying a sentencing statute that was unconstitutional on non-severable terms was not harmless.


OUTCOME: Judgment affirmed.

20 of 2746 DOCUMENTS


IA Constr. Corp. v. Workers' Comp. Appeal Bd. Rhodes


No. 18 WAP 2015


SUPREME COURT OF PENNSYLVANIA


635 Pa. 551; 139 A.3d 154; 2016 Pa. LEXIS 1070


April 5, 2016, Argued 
May 25, 2016, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Costs and fees proceeding at IA Constr. Corp. v. Workers' Comp. Appeal Bd. (Rhodes), 2016 Pa. LEXIS 1564 (Pa., July 22, 2016)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Order of the Commonwealth Court entered February 19, 2015 at No. 2151 CD 2013, reversing the Order of the Workers' Compensation Appeal Board entered November 5, 2013 at No. A11-1631. Intermediate Court Judges: Leadbetter, Bonnie Brigance, Judge; Brobson, P. Kevin, Judge; Colins, James G., Senior Judge.
IA Constr. Corp. v. Workers' Comp. Appeal Bd. (Rhodes), 110 A.3d 1096, 2015 Pa. Commw. LEXIS 76 (Pa. Commw. Ct., 2015)


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: HOLDINGS: [1]-Where claimant suffered traumatic brain injuries in a vehicular accident, Section 306(a.2)(6) of the Pennsylvania Workers' Compensation Act, 77 Pa. Stat. Ann. § 511.2, did not prevent the WCJ from according lesser weight to a doctor's underdeveloped, out-of-specialty opinion regarding the degree of impairment associated with the brain injury; [2]-The doctor's testimony did not elaborate on the differences in impairment attached to the different classes of neurological impairment; [3]-An impairment rating evaluation is entitled to no more or less weight than the results of any other examination; [4]-The WCJ's concern with the doctor's opinion relative to traumatic brain injury served as a sufficient basis for a reasoned rejection of his testimony; [5]-The WCJ was not required to identify substantial contrary evidence in the record to support the rejection.


OUTCOME: Reversed and remanded.

In re Vodvarka


No. 37 MAP 2016


SUPREME COURT OF PENNSYLVANIA


140 A.3d 639; 2016 Pa. LEXIS 1323


April 11, 2016, Submitted 
April 19, 2016, Decided 
June 23, 2016, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: As Corrected on June 27, 2016.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal from the Order of the Commonwealth Court at No. 126 MD 2016 dated March 30, 2016. Other Court Judges: Renee Cohn Jubelirer, Judge; Mary Hannah Leavitt, President Judge; Robert E. Simpson, Judge; Kevin P. Brobson, Judge; Patricia A. McCullough, Judge; Anne E. Covey, Judge; Michael H. Wojcik, Judge.
In re Nomination Petition of Vodvarka, 135 A.3d 1017, 2016 Pa. LEXIS 822 (Pa., Apr. 19, 2016)
In re Vodvarka, 135 A.3d 246, 2016 Pa. Commw. LEXIS 158 (Pa. Commw. Ct., 2016)


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: ISSUE: Whether individuals who continued to reside in the named county but not at the same address as the one listed in the Commonwealth's Statewide Uniform Registry of Electors (SURE) registry satisfied § 2868 of the Pennsylvania Election Code, 25 Pa. Stat. Ann. § 2868. HOLDINGS: [1]-The commonwealth court erred in setting aside a candidate's nomination petition because the failure to file a removal notice, without more, did not result in cancellation of a voter's registration, and thus, no basis existed for a matching address requirement for nominating petitions; [2]-The only basis for striking the signatures on the nominating petition was that the addresses did not match the address on record in the SURE system; [3]-No provision in the Election Code or in Act 2002-3 mandated that the address provided on a nominating petition had to match the address in the SURE system.


OUTCOME: Order reversed.

Markham v. Wolf


No. 59 MAP 2015, No. 60 MAP 2015


SUPREME COURT OF PENNSYLVANIA


635 Pa. 288; 136 A.3d 134; 2016 Pa. LEXIS 690; 206 L.R.R.M. 3034

Markham v. Wolf, 2015 Pa. Commw. Unpub. LEXIS 952 (2015)


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: HOLDINGS: [1]-State legislators lacked standing to intervene in a challenge to an executive order concerning direct care health workers, as the legislators' interests purportedly impacted by the order did not involve unique legislative prerogatives, but were interests common to the general citizenry which only remotely impacted the legislators' right to act as legislators, and their claim that the executive branch of government was diluting the substance of a statutory provision was not an injury which they had standing to pursue.


OUTCOME: The order denying the application to intervene was affirmed.

Commonwealth v. Williams

CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: HOLDINGS: [1]-The Pennsylvania Supreme Court invoked its King's Bench authority under 42 Pa.C.S. § 502 to review whether the Governor's grant of an inmate's reprieve from the death penalty was within his authority, as the Commonwealth showed that the issue was one of significant public importance and that it required timely intervention by the Court; [2]-The Pennsylvania Governor acted within his constitutional authority under Pa. Joseph v. Scranton Times L.P.

PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Order of Superior Court at No. 929 MDA 2012 dated March 11, 2014, Reconsideration Denied May 13, 2014, Vacating and Remanding the decision of the Luzerne County Court of Common Pleas, Civil Division, at No. 2002-3816C judgment entered April 23, 2012.
Joseph v. Scranton Times, L.P., 2014 PA Super 49, 89 A.3d 251, 2014 Pa. Super. LEXIS 123 (Pa. Super. Ct., 2014)


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: HOLDINGS: [1]-In a discretionary appeal concerning a defamation case, the proof presented to show actual malice, including an individual's admission that he relied upon information from six confidential sources in order to write the newspaper articles at issue, could not constitutionally sustain a judgment for presumed or punitive damages in favor of appellees under the First Amendment; the evidence against appellants supported, at most, a finding of negligence; [2]-The Superior Court erred in determining a new trial was warranted to further consider appellees' claims of emotional distress, mental anguish, and personal humiliation; [3]-The record supported the trial judge's conclusion that appellees failed to meet their burden of proving they suffered reputational injury in connection with the publication of the articles, and the Superior Court erred in failing to defer thereto.

27 of 2746 DOCUMENTS


Commonwealth v. Olivo


No. 127 MAP 2014


SUPREME COURT OF PENNSYLVANIA


633 Pa. 617; 127 A.3d 769; 2015 Pa. LEXIS 2673


May 5, 2015, Argued 
November 18, 2015, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Order of the Berks County Court of Common Pleas, Criminal Division, at No. CP-06-CR-0004662-2012 dated August 27, 2013.


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: HOLDINGS: [1]-42 Pa.C.S. § 5920 is clearly a rule of evidence, which the Supreme Court of Pennsylvania has acknowledged can be "governed by statute"; [2]-Moreover, the Court concluded that 42 Pa.C.S. § 5920 is substantive rather than procedural as it permits both parties to present experts to "testify to facts and opinions regarding specific types of victim responses and victim behaviors". It does not dictate how the evidence is presented; [3]-42 Pa.C.S. § 5920 does not provide for the manner of the presentation of expert testimony but merely provides the substantive authorization to present that testimony. Accordingly, 42 Pa.C.S. § 5920 is a substantive rule of evidence that does not violate the Court's Pa. Const. art. V, § 10(c) authority over procedural rules; [4]-42 Pa.C.S. § 5920 does not violate the Court's decision in Dunkle.


OUTCOME: The Court reversed the decision of the trial court suspending 42 Pa.C.S. § 5920 and remanded for further proceedings.

Sernovitz v. Dershaw


No. 123 MAP 2014, No. 124 MAP 2014


SUPREME COURT OF PENNSYLVANIA


633 Pa. 641; 127 A.3d 783; 2015 Pa. LEXIS 2660


May 6, 2015, Argued 
November 18, 2015, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Order of Superior Court at No. 239 EDA 2012 dated 11/14/12, reconsideration denied 1/25/13, reversing, reinstating, and remanded the order of the Montgomery County Court of Common Pleas, Civil Division, at No. 2010-24713 dated 12/20/11. Appeal from the Order of Superior Court at No. 239 EDA 2012 dated 11/14/12, reconsideration denied 1/25/13, reversing, reinstating, and remanded the order of the Montgomery County Court of Common Pleas, Civil Division, at No. 2010-24713 dated 12/20/11.
Sernovitz v. Dershaw, 2012 PA Super 248, 57 A.3d 1254, 2012 Pa. Super. LEXIS 3487 (Pa. Super. Ct., 2012)


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: HOLDINGS: [1]-The superior court erred in severing portions of 1988 Pa. Laws 47 (Act 47), including 42 Pa.C.S. § 8305, because even if Act 47 contained more than one subject in violation of Pa. Const. art. III, § 3, the substantially belated nature of parents' challenge, which arose 22 years after its enactment, rendered the legislation immune to attack on that basis; [2]-Where reliance on the law continued for more than 20 years, a presumption naturally arose that any process challenge was too stale to be cognizable regardless of whether the challengers exercised reasonable diligence; [3]-Invalidating all of the provisions retroactive to 1988 would be unduly disruptive to the orderly administration of justice in Pennsylvania, and doing so would cause greater harm to the public weal than the alleged constitutional transgression itself.


OUTCOME: Order reversed and matter remanded for reinstatement of order dismissing complaint.

CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: HOLDINGS: [1]-The Commonwealth provided sufficient evidence to prove each element of first degree murder, a violation of 18 Pa.C.S. § 2502, beyond a reasonable doubt; [2]-Any error was harmless in denying exclusion of evidence related to four guns, which were seized from defendant's residence immediately after he shot a police officer, but were not used in the commission of the crime; [3]-Defendant admitted at trial he shot the officer, and his defense was centered on his alleged lack of specific intent to kill. OUTCOME: Conviction and sentence affirmed.

Commonwealth v. Hopkins

SUPREME COURT OF PENNSYLVANIA

June 15, 2015, Decided

Commonwealth v. Fisher, 118 A.3d 458, 2015 Pa. Super. Unpub. LEXIS 3317 (2015)


CASE SUMMARY:

40 of 2746 DOCUMENTS


Banfield v. Cortés


No. 83 MAP 2013


SUPREME COURT OF PENNSYLVANIA


631 Pa. 229; 110 A.3d 155; 2015 Pa. LEXIS 358


September 10, 2014, Argued 
February 17, 2015, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Notice of Judgment of Commonwealth Court entered at No. 442 MD 2006 entered October 15, 2013 in favor of Respondent and against petitioners on Counts I, II, III, IV, V, VI, VII, VIII, IX and X of the Petition for Review.

Other Court Judge: Bonnie Brigance Leadbetter, Judge.
Banfield v. Cortes, 922 A.2d 36, 2007 Pa. Commw. LEXIS 170 (Pa. Commw. Ct., 2007)


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: HOLDINGS: [1]-Nothing in the Election Code required an electronic voting system to print a paper ballot for each individual voter to view; rather, the plain language of 25 Pa. Stat. Ann. § 3031.1 required that it had to "provide for" a permanent physical record, which the direct-recording electronic voting systems (DREs) at issue did because they were able to print individual vote records at the close of an election; [2]-DREs were capable of performing a statistical recount as required by 25 Pa. Stat. Ann. § 3031.17; [3]-DREs precluded tampering as required by 25 Pa. Stat. Ann. § 3031.7(16), as the mere possibility of error could not bar the use of a voting system; [4]-DREs that registered votes electronically without a voter-verified ballot did not severely restrict the right to vote or result in disparate treatment in violation of Pa. Const. art. I, § 5 and Pa. Const. art. VII, § 6.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order.

SUPREME COURT OF PENNSYLVANIA


630 Pa. 455; 107 A.3d 29; 2014 Pa. LEXIS 3457


April 8, 2014, Argued 
December 29, 2014, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Order of the Superior Court entered February 27, 2013 at No. 1046 WDA 2012, affirming the Order of the Court of Common Pleas of Mercer County entered June 8, 2012 at No. CP-43-CR-0001291-2011.  [***1] Appeal allowed July 31, 2013 at 152 WAL 2013. Commonwealth v. Dunnavant, 2013 PA Super 38, 63 A.3d 1252, 2013 Pa. Super. LEXIS 83 (Pa. Super. Ct., 2013)


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: HOLDINGS: [1]-In a case involving the admissibility at a criminal trial of evidence consisting of a soundless videotape of a drug deal, captured by a hidden camera police placed in the clothing of a confidential informant, who was invited inside appellee's residence and the drug buy transpired, the Court reversed the judgment of the trial court suppressing the videotape; [2]-The Court held that given the exigent circumstances, and given that there was no underlying unlawful governmental conduct, such as sending a confidential informant into a citizen's home for the purpose of recording a conversation, no constitutional violation occurred.


OUTCOME: Order reversed.

PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Order entered on June 29, 2012 in the Court of Common Pleas of Allegheny County, Criminal Division, at No. CP-02-CR-0015480-1994. Trial Court Judge: Jeffrey A. Manning, Judge.
Commonwealth v. Watkins, 2012 Pa. Dist. & Cnty. Dec. LEXIS 383 (2012)


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: HOLDINGS: [1]-Denial of a petition pursuant to Pennsylvania's Post Conviction Relief Act (PCRA), 42 Pa.C.S. §§ 9541-46, was affirmed, as the PCRA court's conclusions with regard to appellant's competence were supported by the record; appellant's assertion that trial counsel was ineffective for failing to raise appellant's alleged inability and incompetence to waive his Miranda rights due to his brain injury, as a basis for suppression, was unsupported by any credible evidence; [2]-Appellant had not shown a reasonable probability that the outcome of the trial would have been different if only counsel had discovered FBI files; [3]-Photographs of appellant as a young child were not relevant to any mitigating circumstance, and even if they were, the notion that the admission of the photographs would have altered the penalty phase outcome was far-fetched.

Commonwealth v. Blakeney

December 11, 2012, Submitted 
December 29, 2014, Decided

PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Order entered on 1/31/12 in the Court of Common Pleas, Criminal Division of Dauphin County at No. CP-22-CR-0001773-2000. Trial Court Judge: John F. Cherry, Judge.
Commonwealth v. Blakeney, 596 Pa. 510, 946 A.2d 645, 2008 Pa. LEXIS 532 (2008)


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: HOLDINGS: [1]-The trial court properly denied an inmate's petition for relief under the Post Conviction Relief Act, 42 Pa.C.S. §§ 9541-9546, because his claims regarding his alleged incompetency were not supported by the evidence, based on the trial court's observations of the inmate's actions and demeanor and a mental health report which deemed him competent pursuant to 50 Pa. Stat. Ann. § 7402; [2]-Moreover, there was no error in allowing the inmate to proceed pro se because he had not been diagnosed as suffering from a serious mental illness and there was no concern, upon observation of him, as to his competence; [3]-Many claims raised by the inmate as to appellate counsel's ineffectiveness lacked merit and did not require a hearing because they were either waived, previously litigated, or insufficiently presented.


OUTCOME: Order affirmed.

Commonwealth v. Rivera

SUPREME COURT OF PENNSYLVANIA

December 29, 2014, Decided

Commonwealth v. Rivera, 603 Pa. 340, 983 A.2d 1211, 2009 Pa. LEXIS 2490 (2009)


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: HOLDINGS: [1]-In a capital case involving the murder of a police officer, appellant's petition for post-conviction relief was properly dismissed because there were no genuine issues of material fact and no meritorious issues as it was not unreasonable for trial counsel to present appellant's testimony in support of a self-defense claim in the absence of corroborative expert testimony of his mental illness as not such expert testimony was required; [2]-The Court further held that the post conviction court did not abuse its discretion by denying post-conviction discovery since trial counsel had already presented to the jury evidence of police policies regarding officer identification and foot pursuits, and appellant failed to demonstrate that any additional policies on those subjects were relevant.

Commonwealth v. Davido

Commonwealth v. All That Certain Lot Or Parcel of Land Located at 605 Univ. Drive

628 Pa. 434; 104 A.3d 411; 2014 Pa. LEXIS 3026

November 19, 2014, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the order of the Commonwealth Court dated November 21, 2012 at No. 789 CD 2011 reversing the order of the Centre County Court of Common Pleas dated April 15, 2011 at No. CP-14-MD-1134-2009 and remanding to the trial court. Grine, David E., President Judge, Trial Court Judge. Pellegrini, Dan, President Judge, McGinley, Bernard L., Judge, Leadbetter, Bonnie Brigance, Judge, Cohn Jubelirer, Renee, Judge, Leavitt, Mary Hannah, Judge, Brobson, P. Kevin, Judge, McCullough, Patricia A., Judge, Intermediate Court Judges. 61 A.3d 1048 [***1] .
Commonwealth v. 605 University Drive, 61 A.3d 1048, 2012 Pa. Commw. LEXIS 321 (Pa. Commw. Ct., 2012)


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: ISSUE: Whether the intermediate appellate court erred in reversing the trial court's order granting the Commonwealth summary judgment in its petition for forfeiture of appellee's property under the Controlled Substances Forfeiture Act. HOLDINGS: [1]-The intermediate appellate court erred by ruling that the Rules of Civil Procedure inapplicable to forfeiture proceedings; as such proceedings they were civil in nature, where procedural issues arose that could not be resolved solely by application of the Act, the Rules could be used to regulate the practice and procedure; [2]-The intermediate appellate court erred in holding that 42 Pa.C.S. § 6802(i) mandated a hearing in every case before property was forfeited; if the property owner failed to make the necessary claim to the property and to aver that he could establish his claim at the evidentiary hearing, a hearing was not required.


OUTCOME: The intermediate appellate court's order was reversed and the trial court's order was reinstated.

November 19, 2014, Decided

CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: HOLDINGS: [1]-The intermediate appellate court properly affirmed the trial court's reduction of appellant's $14 million damage award against a school district to conform with 42 Pa.C.S. § 8553's $ 500,000 cap on damages available in tort from a local agency. That the damages cap distinguished between those suing public tortfeasors and those suing private defendants did not violate equal protection; the intermediate scrutiny test was met through the damages cap's relationship to legitimate governmental goals in preserving the financial viability of local agencies; [2]-Pa. Const. art. III, § 18 did not undermine the legislature's authority under Pa. Const. art. I, § 11 to limit the amount of recovery in tort actions against governmental entities; [3]-In adopting the damages cap, the legislature did not usurp the judiciary's authority to grant remittitur in individual cases.


OUTCOME: The intermediate appellate court's order was affirmed.

Friends of Pa. Leadership Charter Sch. v. Chester County Bd. of Assessment Appeals

September 24, 2014, Decided

Trial Court Judge: Mark L. Tunnell, Judge. Intermediate Ct. Judges: Renee Cohn Jubelirer, Judge, Patricia A. McCullough, Judge, James G. Colins, Senior Judge. 61 A.3d 354 [***1] .
Friends of Pa. Leadership Charter Sch. v. Chester County Bd. of Assessment Appeals, 61 A.3d 354, 2013 Pa. Commw. LEXIS 23 (Pa. Commw. Ct., 2013)


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: ISSUE: Whether the retroactive tax exemption provided in 24 Pa. Stat. Ann. § 17-1722-A(e)(3) was constitutional, and whether a charter school was entitled to a refund of taxes paid prior to the enactment of the statute. HOLDINGS: [1]-Retroactive application of the real estate tax exemption of 24 Pa. Stat. Ann. § 17-1722-A(e)(3) was unconstitutional under the Pennsylvania Constitution because it violated the separation of powers doctrine by retroactively exempting the charter school's property from real estate taxes when a previous final judgment held that the property was taxable; [2]-The legislation was, in operation and effect, a legislative command to open a final judgment and to have the rights and obligations resolved in that final judgment reassessed in accord with the subsequently expressed legislative will.


OUTCOME: Order affirmed.

Reading Area Water Auth. v. Schuylkill River Greenway Ass'n


No. 62 MAP 2013


SUPREME COURT OF PENNSYLVANIA


627 Pa. 357; 100 A.3d 572; 2014 Pa. LEXIS 2499


March 12, 2014, Argued 
September 24, 2014, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Order of the Commonwealth Court dated July 30, 2012, reconsideration denied September 18, 2012 at No. 1423 CD 2011 which reversed/remanded the order of Berks County Court of Common Pleas, Civil Division, dated June 30, 2011 at No. 10-8544. Trial Court Judge: Jeffrey L. Schmehl, President Judge. Intermediate Ct. Judges: Bonnie Brigance Leadbetter, Judge, Mary Hannah Leavitt, Judge, James G. Colins, Senior Judge.
Reading Area Water Auth. v. Schuylkill River Greenway Ass'n, 50 A.3d 255, 2012 Pa. Commw. LEXIS 225 (Pa. Commw. Ct., 2012)


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: ISSUE: Whether a municipal authority could exercise its eminent domain powers to condemn an easement over privately-owned land, where the sole purpose of the easement was to supply a private developer with land to install sewer drainage facilities needed for a proposed private residential subdivision. HOLDINGS: [1]-The condemnation of the drainage easement fell within the prohibitive scope of 26 Pa.C.S. § 204(a) because whatever public benefit might ensue from the drainage easement, it was being taken to be used for private enterprise; [2]-The municipal authority was not a public utility under the Public Utility Code, so the exception of 26 Pa.C.S. § 204(b)(2)(i) did not apply and the condemnation of the drainage easement was in violation of Pennsylvania's Property Rights Protection Act.


OUTCOME: The order of the Commonwealth Court was reversed, and the matter was remanded to the common pleas court for reinstatement of its order sustaining the preliminary objections and dismissing the complaint.

Commonwealth v. Perez

SUPREME COURT OF PENNSYLVANIA


625 Pa. 601; 93 A.3d 829; 2014 Pa. LEXIS 2220


September 15, 2011, Argued 
June 16, 2014, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: US Supreme Court certiorari denied by Perez v. Pa., 135 S. Ct. 480, 190 L. Ed. 2d 364, 2014 U.S. LEXIS 7627 (U.S., Nov. 10, 2014)

Commonwealth v. Perez, 2008 Pa. Dist. & Cnty. Dec. LEXIS 160 (2008)


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: HOLDINGS: [1]-On mandatory death penalty review, 42 Pa.C.S. § 9711(h), the court held that the Commonwealth produced sufficient evidence to prove each element of first degree murder, 18 Pa.C.S. § 2502(a), beyond a reasonable doubt where defendant admitted to the police that he killed one victim and expressed concern to a fellow inmate about consequences he would face for killing the second victim, a child, and where forensic evidence placed him at the scene of the crime and negated his version of events; [2]-Sufficient evidence supported a finding of aggravating circumstances under 42 Pa.C.S. § 9711(d)(11) and (d)(16) beyond a reasonable doubt, as the two murders were part of the same criminal episode and one victim was under 12; [3]-Death sentence was not a product of passion, prejudice, or any arbitrary factor; [4]-Effectiveness of counsel claims had to be made on collateral review.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the death sentences.

Commonwealth v. Baumhammers


No. 640 CAP


SUPREME COURT OF PENNSYLVANIA


625 Pa. 354; 92 A.3d 708; 2014 Pa. LEXIS 1338


February 19, 2013, Submitted 
May 27, 2014, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Order entered (orally from the bench) on September 14, 2011 in the Court of Common Pleas, Criminal Division of Allegheny County at Nos. CP-02-CR-0014712-2000, CP-02-CR-0014713-2000 and CP-02-CR-0014714-2000 (with the trial court entering its written order on September 23, 2011). Trial Court Judge: Jeffrey A. Manning, Judge.
Commonwealth v. Baumhammers, 2012 Pa. Dist. & Cnty. Dec. LEXIS 363 (2012)


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: HOLDINGS: [1]-The denial of the inmate's claims under the Post Conviction Relief Act, 42 Pa.C.S. §§ 9541-9546 (PCRA), was proper because there were no grounds to disturb the PCRA court's decision to credit a psychiatrist's testimony to the effect that his post-trial characterization of the inmate as suffering from schizophrenia was a mistake. That decision was supported by the record, and as such, the supreme court was bound by it. Accordingly, the psychiatrist's now-disavowed out-of-court statements could not form the basis of a meritorious constitutional claim; [2]-The inmate failed to prove that counsel was ineffective because counsel used reasonable professional skill and subjected the psychiatrist to meaningful adversarial testing.


OUTCOME: Judgment affirmed.

In re Guzzardi


No. 29 MAP 2014


SUPREME COURT OF PENNSYLVANIA


627 Pa. 1; 99 A.3d 381; 2014 Pa. LEXIS 2088


April 21, 2014, Submitted 
May 1, 2014, Decided 
August 18, 2014, Opinion Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Order of the Commonwealth Court at No. 158 MD 2014 dated 4/15/14.
In re Guzzardi, 625 Pa. 336, 91 A.3d 701, 2014 Pa. LEXIS 1142 (Pa., 2014)


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: HOLDINGS: [1]-The trial court erred in denying appellants' objections to a candidate's nomination petition due to his untimely statement of financial interests on the ground that his non-negligent explanations justified treating his late-filed statement nunc pro tunc. Pennsylvania courts could not employ principles of equity to override 65 Pa.C.S. § 1104(b)(3)'s express command that the failure of a candidate for statewide public office to file a timely statement of financial interests with the Ethics Commission was a fatal defect to a petition to appear on the ballot; [2]-In re Nomination Petition of Howells, 20 A.3d 617 (Pa. Cmwlth.), and its line of cases were overruled to the extent they held that where the legislature attached specific consequences to particular acts or omissions, Pennsylvania courts could mitigate the legislatively prescribed outcome through recourse to equity.


OUTCOME: The judgment was reversed.

McCullough, Judge, Anne E. Covey, Judge.

OUTCOME: Judgment reversed and remanded for review pursuant to the substantial evidence standard.

OUTCOME: The order of the intermediate appellate court was reversed.

CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: HOLDINGS: [1]-In a medical malpractice case, Superior Court did not err by generally rejecting "error in judgment" instructions, i.e., instructions that physicians are not liable for errors in judgment when making medical decisions, because such instructions pose palpable and substantial risks of confusing juries with respect to the standard of care in medical malpractice cases, and appellants illustrated the lack of any necessity to use such instructions; [2]-Superior Court's legal conclusion that appellees were prejudiced by the error in judgment instruction, and therefore a new trial was warranted, was considered within the appropriate context of a comprehensive review of the jury charge; [3]-Superior Court properly applied its holding in Pringle outlawing such instructions to this case because, while it was new law, all relevant factors weighed in favor of retroactive application.


OUTCOME: Superior Court order affirmed.

Commonwealth v. Neiman


No. 74 MAP 2011


SUPREME COURT OF PENNSYLVANIA


624 Pa. 53; 84 A.3d 603; 2013 Pa. LEXIS 3018


September 11, 2012, Argued 
December 16, 2013, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: As Amended March 14, 2014.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Appeal from the Order of the Superior Court entered on September 8, 2010 at No. 1747 MDA 2007 affirming the Judgment of Sentence of the Court of Common Pleas of Schuylkill County, Criminal Division, entered on September 27, 2007 at Nos. 1870 and 1871-2005. Trial Court Judge: William E. Baldwin, President Judge.
Commonwealth v. Neiman, 2010 PA Super 162, 5 A.3d 353, 2010 Pa. Super. LEXIS 3220 (Pa. Super. Ct., 2010)


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: ISSUE: Whether 2004 Pa. Laws § 1243, No. 152 (Act 152), amending the Judicial Code, 42 Pa.C.S. §§ 101 - 9913, violated the "single subject" rule of Pa. Const. art. III, § 3, and, if so, whether amendments to 42 Pa.C.S. § 9791 et seq. (Megan's Law), was severable. HOLDINGS: [1]-Act 152 violated Pa. Const. art. III, § 3 because the fact it amended 42 Pa.C.S. §§ 101 - 9913 did not satisfy Pa. Const. art. III, § 3, subjects of refining civil remedies or relief and judicial remedies and sanctions were too broad, and provisions on deficiency judgment procedures, asbestos statutes of limitations, county police jurisdiction, and sexual offender registration requirements did not act together as a unifying scheme to accomplish one purpose; [2]-Megan's Law provisions could not be severed because all Act 152's provisions were equally void, so one did not offend the Constitution more than another.


OUTCOME: Judgment reversed.

OUTCOME: Decision reversed.

91 of 2746 DOCUMENTS


Friedman v. Corbett


No. 39 MAP 2013


SUPREME COURT OF PENNSYLVANIA


620 Pa. 569; 72 A.3d 255; 2013 Pa. LEXIS 1539



July 16, 2013, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Plenary Jurisdiction assumed from Commonwealth Court at No. 81 MD 2013.
Friedman v. Corbett, 620 Pa. 213, 66 A.3d 763, 2013 Pa. LEXIS 944 (Pa., 2013)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioners, judges and voters, sought alleged in the Commonwealth Court (Pennsylvania), that Pa. Const. art. V. § 16(b) violated Pa. Const. art. I. The Pennsylvania Supreme Court assumed plenary jurisdiction, under 42 Pa.C.S. § 726, and petitioners filed an application for relief, requesting the appointment of a special master. Respondent, the Commonwealth of Pennsylvania, opposed and filed preliminary objections in the nature of a demurrer.


OVERVIEW: Petitioners wanted a master to hear evidence. The supreme court held evidence of demographic changes was unnecessary because it did not affect the issue, since further constitutional amendment should account for such changes. Evidence the retirement mandate was irrational was unnecessary because that conclusion had been rejected. Evidence on voters' understanding when voting for a judge was irrelevant because (1) they were deemed to know terms of judges who had to retire would expire early, (2) their contrary understanding did not support their claim, as an uninformed vote counted, and no ballot deficiency showed unconstitutionality, and (3) voters had no inherent right to vote for candidates unaffected by the provision. The Commonwealth's demurrer succeeded because (1) all but two of petitioners' claims had been rejected, (2) a claim that voters had a right to enjoy a judge's "full service" was rejected in denying the application for relief, and (2) changing a judge's retirement date to December 31st of the year in which the judge turned 70 was not irrational, as it improved orderly judicial succession, reduced vacancies from mid-year retirements, and was minimally discriminatory.


OUTCOME: The application for relief was denied, the Commonwealth's demurrer was sustained, and the petition was dismissed with prejudice.

 

92 of 2746 DOCUMENTS


Driscoll v. Corbett


No. 19 MAP 2013, No. 20 MAP 2013


SUPREME COURT OF PENNSYLVANIA


620 Pa. 494; 69 A.3d 197; 2013 Pa. LEXIS 1254; 118 Fair Empl. Prac. Cas. (BNA) 1574


May 8, 2013, Argued 
June 17, 2013, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: As Corrected June 18, 2013.
Related proceeding at Lerner v. Corbett, 972 F. Supp. 2d 676, 2013 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 136425 (M.D. Pa., Sept. 24, 2013)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Extraordinary Relief was granted from Commonwealth Court at 43 MD 2013.

Extraordinary Relief was granted from Commonwealth Court at 48 MD 2013.
Driscoll v. Corbett, 619 Pa. 400, 64 A.3d 629, 2013 Pa. LEXIS 592 (Pa., 2013)
Tilson v. Corbett, 619 Pa. 399, 64 A.3d 628, 2013 Pa. LEXIS 591 (Pa., 2013)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioners judges sued respondents state officials in the Commonwealth Court (Pennsylvania) to nullify the mandatory judicial retirement provision of Pa. Const. art. V, § 16(b). After initiating proceedings in the Commonwealth Court, the judges sought extraordinary relief in the Pennsylvania Supreme Court, which granted their application to assume plenary jurisdiction under 42 Pa.C.S. § 726.


OVERVIEW: The judges said the provision was subject to heightened review. The supreme court disagreed because (1) a constitutional provision was strongly presumed to be inherently constitutional, so judicial review was highly deferential, and (2) given the need to balance equal protection against the right to amend the Constitution, the provision's age-related basis did not implicate such scrutiny. It met conventional rational basis review because (1) there was no compelling reason to depart from precedent so holding, and (2) it was not so unrelated to achieving legitimate purposes that it could be concluded that the people's actions in adopting it were irrational. It did not violate the anti-discrimination protections of Pa. Const. art. I, § 26 because (1) Pa. Const. art. I, § 26 was of recent vintage, so a claim that it enshrined rights pre-existing the Constitution was not compelling, and (2) Pa. Const. art. I, § 26 was approved substantially contemporaneously with Pa. Const. art. V, § 16 (2001), so the former was not likely intended to forbid the latter. The provision did not offend due process because judges had no property interest in serving past their constitutional retirement date.


OUTCOME: The matter was remanded to the Commonwealth Court for dismissal of the complaints with prejudice and entry of judgment in favor of the Commonwealth.

Commonwealth v. Rega


No. 642 CAP


SUPREME COURT OF PENNSYLVANIA


620 Pa. 640; 70 A.3d 777; 2013 Pa. LEXIS 1251

June 17, 2013, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1]

Commonwealth v. Rega, 598 Pa. 185, 955 A.2d 345, 2008 Pa. LEXIS 1269 (2008)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant inmate sought review of an order of the Court of Common Pleas, Criminal Division of Jefferson County (Pennsylvania), which denied his petition under the Post Conviction Relief Act (PCRA), 42 Pa.C.S. §§ 9541-9546. The inmate had been convicted of, inter alia, first-degree murder, and he was sentenced to death.


OVERVIEW: The inmate was involved in a conspiracy to perpetrate a robbery at a lodge. In the course of the incident, the inmate shot and killed a night watchman. He was convicted of first-degree murder and other offenses, and he was sentenced to death. Eventually, the judgment of sentence was affirmed on direct appeal. The inmate's PCRA petition was denied after evidentiary hearings. On appeal, the court found no violation under Brady, as the evidence supported the finding that no there were no promises made to prosecution witnesses who were co-perpetrators in the criminal incident. Despite multiple assertions by the inmate, there was no ineffectiveness shown in counsel's questioning of witnesses, failure to object to after-hours trial sessions, or in other regards. The aggravator under 42 Pa.C.S. § 9711(d)(9) was clearly applicable, and an instruction on § 9711(d)(6) was appropriately provided.

Northwestern Youth Servs. v. Commonwealth, Dep't of Pub. Welfare


No. 48 MAP 2010


SUPREME COURT OF PENNSYLVANIA


620 Pa. 140; 66 A.3d 301; 2013 Pa. LEXIS 792


September 13, 2011, Argued 
April 24, 2013, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Appeal from the Order of the Commonwealth Court at No. 386 MD 2009 dated July 23, 2010.
Northwestern Youth Servs. v. Commonwealth Dep't of Pub. Welfare, 1 A.3d 988, 2010 Pa. Commw. LEXIS 400 (Pa. Commw. Ct., 2010)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellees non-profit entities alleged that changes effected by administrative bulletins were ultra vires and unconstitutional or that appellant Department of Public Welfare (DPW) failed to comply with mandatory regulatory-review procedures designed to ensure a meaningful opportunity for public participation and independent regulatory oversight. DPW challenged a judgment entered for the entities in the Commonwealth Court (Pennsylvania).


OVERVIEW: The entities furnished out-of-home child welfare and/or juvenile justice services under county contracts. They challenged changes to DPW's practices and policies in determining appropriate reimbursement of county expenditures for out-of-home, child-welfare placement services, arguing that DPW, through a series of recent administrative bulletins, had unilaterally and inappropriately substituted a restrictive, statewide rate-setting process in place of the prior regime. The supreme court held that the commonwealth court did not err in concluding that the bulletin contained procedurally invalid legislative regulations. The bulletin was practically binding, or binding enough. The availability of federal and state funding very often would be of critical importance in the local decision-making. The Legislature did not wholly relieve DPW of compliance with all of the formalities attending legislative rule-making in the child-welfare arena, and nothing in the Public Welfare Code or the derivative regulations persuaded the supreme court that the policy shift manifested in the bulletin could be fairly denominated as a mere interpretation of pre-existing legislative rules.


OUTCOME: The supreme court affirmed the judgment.

 

95 of 2746 DOCUMENTS


Commonwealth v. Batts


No. 79 MAP 2009


SUPREME COURT OF PENNSYLVANIA


620 Pa. 115; 66 A.3d 286; 2013 Pa. LEXIS 519


September 12, 2012, Argued 
March 26, 2013, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Decision reached on appeal by Commonwealth v. Batts, 2015 PA Super 187, 2015 Pa. Super. LEXIS 508 (Pa. Super. Ct., 2015)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Appeal from the Order of the Superior Court at No. 766 EDA 2008 dated April 7, 2009 affirming the judgment of sentence of Northampton County Court of Common Pleas, Criminal Division, at No. 1215-2006 dated October 22, 2007. Trial Court Judge: William F. Moran, Judge.
Commonwealth v. Batts, 974 A.2d 1175, 2009 Pa. Super. LEXIS 2322 (Pa. Super. Ct., 2009)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant, a juvenile, appealed a decision of the Superior Court (Pennsylvania), which affirmed a trial court judgment of sentence of a mandatory life-without-parole sentence for defendant's conviction of first-degree murder under former 18 Pa.C.S. § 1102(a)(1) (superseded by 18 Pa.C.S. § 1102.1). He was also convicted and sentenced on other charges. Defendant was under the age of 18 years at the time of the offense.


OVERVIEW: Defendant fatally shot one victim and shot another victim who was seriously injured but recovered. At the time, defendant was 14 years old. He indicated that he was forced to do it by a superior gang member. Despite his defense of duress, the jury convicted defendant and he was sentenced to, inter alia, a mandatory term of life imprisonment without parole pursuant to former § 1102(a)(1) and 61 Pa.C.S. § 6137(a)(1). His post-sentence motions were denied. The Superior Court upheld the sentence. On further review and upon consideration of developing jurisprudence, the court noted that judicial consideration of appropriate age-related factors was required prior to imposition of a life-without-parole sentence on a juvenile. Accordingly, the sentence violated U.S. Const. amend. VIII. The appropriate remedy was the imposition of a minimum sentence that took age-appropriate factors into account. A categorical ban on the life-without-parole sentences on juvenile offenders was not required by Pa. Const. art. I, § 13, as it did not require a broader approach to proportionality for juveniles than was reflected in prevailing United States Supreme Court jurisprudence.


OUTCOME: The court vacated the decision of the Superior Court and the matter was remanded to the trial court for further proceedings.

 

96 of 2746 DOCUMENTS


Commonwealth v. Simpson


No. 493 CAP


SUPREME COURT OF PENNSYLVANIA


620 Pa. 60; 66 A.3d 253; 2013 Pa. LEXIS 541


June 3, 2008, Submitted 
March 26, 2013, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Appeal from the on October 18, 2005 in the Court of Common Pleas of Philadelphia County, Criminal Division, denying PCRA relief at No. 9611-0316 1/2. Trial Court Judge: David Savitt, Senior Judge.
Commonwealth v. Simpson, 562 Pa. 255, 754 A.2d 1264, 2000 Pa. LEXIS 1775 (2000)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: After defendant's conviction of first degree murder and sentence to death were affirmed on direct appeal, he filed a petition for relief under the Post Conviction Relief Act, 42 Pa.C.S. § 9541 et seq., on the ground of ineffective assistance of counsel. The Philadelphia County Court of Common Pleas (Pennsylvania) dismissed the petition without a hearing. Defendant challenged the order.


OVERVIEW: The lower court did not err in dismissing defendant's Batson claim where he failed to prove actual, purposeful discrimination in the Commonwealth's exercise of its peremptory challenges. The lower court also properly rejected defendant's Brady claims where, inter alia, any Brady concerns related to the victim's crack cocaine sales had been raised by a codefendant, thereby vitiating any such concerns. Defendant's claim of ineffective counsel was rejected where the jury was informed that a witness had identified another as the person who initially kidnapped the victim, and thus, he failed to show any prejudice as a result of trial counsel's failure in having the witness' entire statement read into the record. However, the lower court's order as to an ineffective counsel claim based on the failure to impeach an eyewitness was vacated where there was no record concerning counsel's strategic basis for the decision not to impeach that witness with evidence of motive and bias or with testimony from another individual concerning defendant's whereabouts during the relevant time period. The remaining ineffective assistance of counsel claims lacked merit.


OUTCOME: The order was affirmed in part and vacated in part. The case was remanded for further proceedings.

 

97 of 2746 DOCUMENTS


Sci. Games Int'l, Inc. v. Commonwealth


No. 42 MAP 2012, No. 43 MAP 2012


SUPREME COURT OF PENNSYLVANIA


620 Pa. 175; 66 A.3d 740; 2013 Pa. LEXIS 518


October 16, 2012, Argued 
March 25, 2013, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Appeal from the Order of the Commonwealth Court at No. 380 MD 2011 dated November 30, 2011 and amended December 22, 2011. Dan Pellegrini, President Judge, Jubelirer Cohn, Judge, James R. Kelley, Senior Judge.

Appeal from the Order of the Commonwealth Court at No. 380 MD 2011 dated November 3, 2011 and amended December 22, 2011. Dan Pellegrini, President Judge, Jubelirer Cohn, Judge, James R. Kelley, Senior Judge.
Sci. Games Int'l, Inc. v. Dep't of Revenue, 34 A.3d 307, 2011 Pa. Commw. LEXIS 590 (Pa. Commw. Ct., 2011)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In an interlocutory appeal by permission, the Commonwealth agencies challenged an order of the Commonwealth Court (Pennsylvania) holding that the court had jurisdiction to consider the bidder's action challenging the cancellation of a request for proposals and seeking declaratory and injunctive relief.


OVERVIEW: Relative to controversies in matters arising from procurement contracts with Commonwealth agencies, the Board of Claims retained exclusive jurisdiction (subject to all jurisdictional prerequisites), which was not to be supplanted by a court of law through an exercise of original jurisdiction. As to challenges to cancellations of solicitations asserted under 62 Pa.C.S. § 521 of the Procurement Code, the legislature did not implement any waiver of sovereign immunity and afforded no remedy to aggrieved bidders and offerors which have not yet entered into an executed contract with a Commonwealth agency. For those attaining the status of contractor, which the court found should be deemed to occur at the time a contract is executed by all parties, the remedial procedure was via 62 Pa.C.S. § 1712.1, subject to review within the exclusive jurisdiction of the Board of Claims. Thus, the Commonwealth Court lacked jurisdiction over the bidder's action against two agencies.


OUTCOME: The order was reversed. The matter was remanded for dismissal consistent with the court's opinion.

Pa. State Ass'n of Jury Comm'rs v. Commonwealth


No. 66 MAP 2012


SUPREME COURT OF PENNSYLVANIA


619 Pa. 369; 64 A.3d 611; 2013 Pa. LEXIS 458


March 5, 2013, Argued 
March 14, 2013, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Subsequent appeal at, Decision reached on appeal by Pa. State Ass'n of Jury Comm'rs v. Commonwealth, 65 A.3d 297, 2013 Pa. LEXIS 737 (Pa., 2013)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Appeal from the Order of the Commonwealth Court, dated July 26, 2012, at No. 21 MD 2012, denying Appellant's Motion for Judgment on the Pleadings and granting Intervenor's Motion for Judgment on the Pleadings. Other Court Judges: P. Kevin Brobson, Judge, Bonnie Brigance Leadbetter, Judge, Bernard L. McGinley, Judge, Robert E. Simpson, Judge, Anne E. Covey, Judge, Mary Hannah Leavitt, Judge, Dan Pellegrini, President Judge.
Pa. State Ass'n of Jury Comm'rs v. Commonwealth, 53 A.3d 109, 2012 Pa. Commw. LEXIS 219 (Pa. Commw. Ct., 2012)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, various jury commissioners and related others, sought review of an order from an en banc panel of the Commonwealth Court (Pennsylvania), which denied their motion for judgment on the pleadings, and granted a motion by intervenor, the County Commissioners Association of Pennsylvania, for judgment on the pleadings. The matter involved constitutional challenges to Act 108 of 2011, 2011 Pa. Laws 442.


OVERVIEW: The initial proposal for 2011 Pa. Laws 442 related to electronic and online sales of personal property and surplus farm equipment. After passing through the legislative process, an additional proposal was included regarding the abolishment of the office of jury commissioner. The bill passed out of the Senate and the House, and was signed into law by the Governor. The jury commissioners sought injunctive and declaratory relief with respect to their constitutional challenges to 2011 Pa. Laws 442. Challenges included that it was violative of the "single subject rule" of Pa. Const. art. III, § 3, the separation of powers doctrine of Pa. Const. art. V, §§ 1 and 10, and the due process clause of U.S. Const. amend. XIV. The Commonwealth Court rejected the constitutional challenges and dismissed the matter. On appeal, the court found that 2011 Pa. Laws 442 was unconstitutional with respect to the single subject challenge. The law sought to combine topics that were not sufficiently germane to each other. The label of "powers of county commissioners" was overly broad and could not be sufficiently narrowed where it included both executive and legislative functions of the board.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the order of the Commonwealth Court and declared the law to be unconstitutional.

Herd Chiropractic Clinic, P.C. v. State Farm Mut. Auto. Ins. Co.


No. 35 MAP 2012


SUPREME COURT OF PENNSYLVANIA


619 Pa. 438; 64 A.3d 1058; 2013 Pa. LEXIS 304


October 16, 2012, Argued 
February 20, 2013, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Appeal from the Order of the Superior Court entered on August 23, 2011 at No. 882 MDA 2010, which affirmed the judgment of Dauphin County Court of Common Pleas, Civil Division, entered on June 29, 2010 at No. 1320 CV 2006. Appeal allowed April 30, 2012 at 625 MAL 2011. Trial Court Judge: Bruce F. Bratton, Judge. Intermediate Court Judges: Jack A. Panella, Anne E. Lazarus, Paula Francisco Ott, JJ.
Herd Chiropractic Clinic, P.C. v. State Farm Mut. Auto. Ins. Co., 2011 PA Super 178, 29 A.3d 19, 2011 Pa. Super. LEXIS 2243 (Pa. Super. Ct., 2011)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant insurer sought review of the judgment of the Superior Court (Pennsylvania) which affirmed a trial court's decision to award attorney fees to appellee provider. The appeal concerned the sustainability of an award of attorneys' fees against an insurance company under the peer-review provisions of the Motor Vehicle Financial Responsibility Law.


OVERVIEW: An individual obtained treatment from the provider for injuries sustained in a motor vehicle accident. The insurer, the automobile insurer for the patient's family, submitted Provider's invoices to a peer review organization (PRO) pursuant to 75 Pa.C.S. § 1797(b). The PRO determined that certain chiropractic treatments were not necessary or reasonable, and the insurer refused to pay for such treatment. The provider then commenced a civil action against the insurer, seeking compensation for unpaid bills in the amount of $1380. The Pennsylvania Supreme Court consistently followed the general, American rule that there could be no recovery of attorneys' fees from an adverse party, absent an express statutory authorization, a clear agreement by the parties, or some other established exception. 75 Pa.C.S. § 1797(b)(4) authorized appeals by providers from insurer refusals to pay for treatment, the reasonableness or necessity of which the insurer had not challenged before a peer review organization. There was simply no express statutory authorization for fee shifting on provider challenges to peer-review determinations.


OUTCOME: The judgment was reversed. The matter was remanded for conformance of the judgment.

 

100 of 2746 DOCUMENTS


Glatfelter Pulpwood Co. v. Commonwealth


No. 62 MAP 2011


SUPREME COURT OF PENNSYLVANIA


619 Pa. 243; 61 A.3d 993; 2013 Pa. LEXIS 106


May 8, 2012, Argued 
January 22, 2013, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Appeal from the Order of Commonwealth Court at No. 362 FR 2007 dated 5/31/11 overruling the exceptions and entering judgment of the 5/4/11 order that affirmed the decision of the Board of Finance and Revenue Order dated 5/22/07 at No. 0618748. Intermediate Court Judge: Barry F. Feudale, Senior Judge.
Glatfelter Pulpwood Co. v. Commonwealth, 19 A.3d 572, 2011 Pa. Commw. LEXIS 216 (Pa. Commw. Ct., 2011)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant taxpayer challenged an order from the Commonwealth Court (Pennsylvania), which affirmed an administrative determination that the taxpayer's gains from the sale of a tract of Delaware timberland was business income subject to taxation in Pennsylvania.


OVERVIEW: The taxpayer, a wholly-owned subsidiary of a Pennsylvania corporation that manufactured paper products, had as its sole business activity procuring pulpwood for its parent company's operations. It owned and managed timberland property. After selling some of its timberland in Delaware, it allocated the entire net gain to Delaware as required by Delaware tax law and paid Delaware corporate income tax on the entire gain. The court held that the gain was business income as defined in 72 Pa. Stat. Ann. § 7401(3)2.(a)(1)(A) under the functional test because the acquisition and the management of the timberland were integral parts of the taxpayer's regular business operations. Because the statute was phrased in the disjunctive, it was immaterial whether the disposition of the timberland was also an integral part of the taxpayer's regular business operations. The court further held that although Delaware already had taxed the entire gain, Pennsylvania's duplicative taxation of a portion of the gain did not violate the Due Process and Commerce Clauses of the United States Constitution because the taxpayer was a unitary business and Pennsylvania's apportionment formula was fairly applied.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order.

Commonwealth v. DeJesus


No. 546 CAP, No. 547 CAP


SUPREME COURT OF PENNSYLVANIA


619 Pa. 70; 58 A.3d 62; 2012 Pa. LEXIS 2892


June 30, 2010, Submitted 
December 14, 2012, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Appeal from the Order entered on August 10, 2007 in the Court of Common Pleas, Criminal Division of Philadelphia County, granting the PCRA petition in part at CP-51-CR-1103501-1997. Appeal from the Order entered on August 10, 2007 in the Court of Common Pleas, Criminal Division of Philadelphia County, denying the PCRA petition in part at CP-51-CR-1103501-1997. Trial Court Judge: Jane Cutler Greenspan, Judge.
Commonwealth v. DeJesus, 567 Pa. 415, 787 A.2d 394, 2001 Pa. LEXIS 2761 (2001)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Commonwealth of Pennsylvania appealed orders of the Court of Common Pleas of Philadelphia County (Pennsylvania), which granted partial relief under the Post Conviction Relief Act (PCRA), 42 Pa.C.S. §§ 9541-9546, and determined that appellee inmate was ineligible for the death penalty due to his mental retardation. The trial court also denied the Commonwealth's motion to reopen. The inmate filed a cross-appeal.


OVERVIEW: The inmate was involved in the shooting deaths of two people and shootings of two other victims who survived. He was convicted of first-degree murder as well as lesser charges. The jury imposed death sentences, and a direct appeal resulted in an affirmance. The inmate sought PCRA relief and asserted an Atkins claim. The Commonwealth's motion to reopen the record, based on evidence that allegedly cast doubt on the inmate's claims of mental retardation due to his use of smuggled cell phones and other conduct, was denied. The PCRA court concluded that the inmate had limited intellectual functioning, and it vacated the death sentences. On appeal, the court determined that for an Atkins claim on collateral review, the preponderance of the evidence standard remained appropriate, and that the use of the factors dictated in Ex Parte Briseno, 135 S.W.3d 1 (Tex. Crim. App. 2004), was helpful in assessing an inmate's adaptive functioning. However, it determined that the trial court abused its discretion in denying the motion to reopen, as the additional evidence was relevant, there was no prejudice to the inmate, and there was a concern as to a fraud perpetrated on the court.


OUTCOME: The court vacated the order of the trial court with respect to the denial of the Commonwealth's motion to reopen, as well as the accompanying order which found the inmate mentally retarded and vacated his death sentences. The remainder of the requested relief was denied, and the matter was remanded for further Atkins proceedings.
