Konidaris v. Portnoff Law Assocs.


Nos. 14 and 15 WAP 2006


SUPREME COURT OF PENNSYLVANIA


598 Pa. 55; 953 A.2d 1231; 2008 Pa. LEXIS 1291


March 5, 2007, Argued 
August 18, 2008, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Appeals from the Order of Commonwealth Court entered September 16, 2005 at No. 2428 CD 2004, affirming in part and reversing in part the Order of the Allegheny County Court of Common Pleas entered September 17, 2004 at No. GD 03-006341. 884 A.2d 348 (Pa. Cmwlth. 2005).
Konidaris v. Portnoff Law Assocs., 884 A.2d 348, 2005 Pa. Commw. LEXIS 521 (Pa. Commw. Ct., 2005)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant delinquent taxpayers and appellee law firm sought review of an order of the Commonwealth Court (Pennsylvania), which affirmed the denial of summary judgment to the taxpayers and reversed the grant of partial summary judgment to the law firm on the issue of the constitutionality of 2003 Pa. Laws 83, No. 20 (Act 20), which retroactively amended 53 Pa. Stat. Ann. § 7106 to permit the collection of attorney's fees in tax claim cases.


OVERVIEW: The taxpayers had failed to pay school taxes for a number of years, and the tax claim was secured by liens on their property. The law firm was retained to collect the delinquent taxes. Attorney's fees were added to the total tax claim. After a decision in another case disallowing the imposition of attorney's fees incident to tax claims prior to the amendment of the Municipal Claims and Tax Liens Act (MCTLA), 53 Pa. Stat. Ann. § 7101 et seq., the taxpayers filed the instant action. The taxpayers claimed that Act 20, allowing collection of attorney's fees in such a case, violated the Remedies Clause, Pa. Const. art. I, § 11. On appeal, the court reversed to the extent a Remedies Clause violation was found. In interpreting Pa. Const. art. I, § 11, the court determined that it had been invoked when a statutory or common law cause of action for an injury had been altered or eliminated in full by the legislature. Although the taxpayers claimed that they would be deprived of a vested right in the nature of a defense, the constitutional protection was for a remedy for an injury done; instead, the taxpayers' claim was for a right not to do something, specifically to pay attorney's fees.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the commonwealth court's decision in part and reinstated the grant of partial summary judgment entered by the trial court in favor of the law firm; the court remanded the action to the trial court for further proceedings, including the determination of a reasonable attorney's fee.

Commonwealth v. Rabold


No. 106 MAP 2007


SUPREME COURT OF PENNSYLVANIA


597 Pa. 344; 951 A.2d 329; 2008 Pa. LEXIS 1178


May 13, 2008, Argued 
July 23, 2008, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Appeal from the Order of the Superior Court entered on 3/8/07 at No. 832 EDA 2006 which Affirmed the Judgment of Sentence of Monroe County Court of Common Pleas, Criminal Division entered on 8/11/05 at No. CR-389-2003. Appeal allowed October 30, 2007 at 291 MAL 2007. Trial Court Judges: Margherita Patti Worthington, Judge. Intermediate Court Judges: Correale F. Stevens, Richard B. Klein, Jack A. Panella, JJ.
Commonwealth v. Rabold, 2007 PA Super 62, 920 A.2d 857, 2007 Pa. Super. LEXIS 309 (Pa. Super. Ct., 2007)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Following a jury trial, defendant was found guilty but mentally ill of attempted homicide, guilty but mentally ill of aggravated assault, and guilty of possession of an instrument of crime. The Superior Court of Pennsylvania affirmed. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant advanced an insanity defense. Two expert witnesses agreed on a diagnosis, but differed on whether defendant was legally insane. The Commonwealth's expert testified that defendant was, at the time of his offenses, "mentally ill" under the definition set forth in 18 Pa.C.S. § 314 because he lacked substantial capacity to conform his conduct to the requirements of the law. The appellate court found that the sole contest initiated by defendant at trial to the jury charge on this issue was limited to his assertion that the burden in connection with a guilty-but-mentally-ill verdict should have been assigned to the Commonwealth on proof beyond a reasonable doubt. The appellate court disagreed. 18 Pa.C.S. § 314(a) did not impose a burden of proof concerning an accused's mental illness on either party, but rather, was implicated where an insanity defense failed but evidence of mental illness nevertheless preponderated. This approach did not remove the burden from the Commonwealth of establishing each element of an offense beyond a reasonable doubt. The burden did not need to be assigned to the Commonwealth to prove defendant's mental illness beyond a reasonable doubt.


OUTCOME: The order of the intermediate appellate court was affirmed.

Commonwealth v. Sam


No. 49 EAP 2005


SUPREME COURT OF PENNSYLVANIA


597 Pa. 523; 952 A.2d 565; 2008 Pa. LEXIS 1175


October 16, 2006, Argued; January 11, 2008, Resubmitted; April 15, 2008, Reargued 
July 22, 2008, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Stay denied by, Request granted Commonwealth v. Sam, 599 Pa. 460, 961 A.2d 1227, 2008 Pa. LEXIS 2189 (2008)
Motion granted by Sam v. Pennsylvania, 129 S. Ct. 1031, 173 L. Ed. 2d 290, 2009 U.S. LEXIS 602 (U.S., 2009)
US Supreme Court certiorari denied by Sam v. Pennsylvania, 130 S. Ct. 50, 175 L. Ed. 2d 42, 2009 U.S. LEXIS 5360 (U.S., Oct. 5, 2009)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Appeal from the Order entered on October 20, 2005 in the Court of Common Pleas, Criminal Division of Philadelphia County, denying Motion to Compel Psychiatric Medication at Nos. 8907-4359 1/1. Trial Court Judge: C. Darnell Jones, II, President Judge.
Commonwealth v. Sam, 535 Pa. 350, 635 A.2d 603, 1993 Pa. LEXIS 290 (1993)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant Commonwealth sought review of an order of the Court of Common Pleas of Philadelphia County (Pennsylvania), which denied a request by the Commonwealth for an order to compel the administration of antipsychotic medication to appellee inmate to determine if the inmate chose to proceed with a request for postconviction relief under the Post Conviction Relief Act, 42 Pa.C.S. §§ 9541-9546.


OVERVIEW: The inmate had received three consecutive death sentences on murder convictions. Subsequently, an attorney, who had not been retained by the inmate, filed a petition under the Act; the attorney asserted that the inmate was not presently competent. The inmate was examined by a psychiatrist for the Commonwealth and a psychologist for the defense and determined to be mentally incompetent. However, the lower court denied the request of the Commonwealth for the administration of antipsychotic medication because allegedly no evidence was presented that the inmate was a danger to himself or others. On appeal, the court reversed. The court concluded that the four-part test in Sell v. United States, 539 U.S. 166 (2003), did not have to be applied as the instant case did not involve a question of whether the inmate was competent to stand trial; the Commonwealth was not required to meet the four strict Sell conditions because it was not seeking an end that was against the inmate's interest. However, because the parties assumed that the four-factor test applied, the court tracked that analysis, finding that the Commonwealth met all four factors, and weighed the distinction in the balance.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the lower court's denial of the Commonwealth's request to compel antipsychotic medication and remanded for further proceedings. If the medication rendered the inmate competent, the lower court was to determine if the inmate wished to proceed with the petition and, if so, whether the inmate could assist counsel. If the inmate was not rendered competent, the lower court was to consider whether the petition should be dismissed.

Commonwealth v. Williams


Nos. 430 & 431 CAP


SUPREME COURT OF PENNSYLVANIA


597 Pa. 109; 950 A.2d 294; 2008 Pa. LEXIS 919


November 29, 2006, Resubmitted 
June 17, 2008, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Appeal from the Order entered on October 17, 2003 granting defendant a new trial in the Court of Common Pleas, Criminal Division of Lehigh County at No. 981/1984. Trial Court Judges: Carol K. McGinley, Judge.

Appeal from the Order entered on October 17, 2003 denying portions of Post Conviction Relief Act relief in the Court of Common Pleas, Criminal Division of Lehigh County at No. 981/1984. Trial Court Judges: Carol K. McGinley, Judge.
Commonwealth v. Williams, 573 Pa. 613, 828 A.2d 981, 2003 Pa. LEXIS 1242 (2003)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In consolidated capital post-conviction cross-appeals, defendant challenged the denial, in part, of postconviction relief from his convictions for first-degree murder and related offenses by Court of Common Pleas of Lehigh County (Pennsylvania) (PCRA court) as to all guilt-phase claims. The Commonwealth sought to overturn the award of a new penalty hearing based upon a finding of ineffective assistance of counsel.


OVERVIEW: Defendant shot and killed the victim, a truck driver. At the pre-trial stage, the public defender was permitted to withdraw. The trial court appointed new counsel subject to a $ 3,500 fee cap and, apparently, a $ 500 limitation on available reimbursement for investigative services. The trial court also rescheduled trial, which commenced 22 days later. At trial, the Commonwealth introduced defendant's confession and testimony from various witnesses. The Pennsylvania Supreme Court concluded that the PCRA court's findings were supported by the evidence and free from legal error. Capital counsel had an obligation to pursue all reasonable avenues for developing mitigating evidence. Given the information available, counsel should have considered the development and presentation of mental-health mitigation at the penalty phase of trial. While the pretrial proceedings were unusual, irregularity, did not necessarily arise to a constitutional violation. The PCRA court did not find that the judge directed a specific and/or irrevocable trial date, and the appellate court did not believe that such finding was inescapable on the present record.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the PCRA court was affirmed.

Appeal from the Order of the Commonwealth Court, entered March 1, 2006, at No. 98 M.D. 2005.Intermediate Court Judges: Bonnie Brigance Leadbetter, President Judge. James Gardner Colins, Doris A. Smith-Ribner, Dan Pellegrini, Rochelle S. Friedman, Renee Jubelirer Cohn, Robert E. Simpson, JJ.

OVERVIEW: Appellee credit unions notified appellee state banking department of an intent to convert their charters to allow membership based on common bonds of geography. VIII, §§ 2 and 5. OUTCOME: The state supreme court quashed the appeal as interlocutory.

Commonwealth v. Brown


No. 162 MAP 2005


SUPREME COURT OF PENNSYLVANIA


596 Pa. 354; 943 A.2d 264; 2008 Pa. LEXIS 264


May 10, 2006, Argued 
March 26, 2008, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Appeal from the Order of the Superior Court at No. 865 MDA 2004 entered on 3/31/05 quashing the order of York County Court of Common Pleas, Criminal Division, at No. 2419 CA 2000 entered on 4/26/04. Trial Court Judges: Kennedy, John S., Judge. Intermediate Court Judges: Klein, Richard B., Judge, McCaffery, Seamus P., Judge, Montemuro Frank, J., Judge.
Commonwealth v. Brown, 875 A.2d 383, 2005 Pa. Super. LEXIS 893 (Pa. Super. Ct., 2005)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of an order of the Superior Court (Pennsylvania), which denied the state postconviction petition for relief filed by appellant.


OVERVIEW: After appellant was convicted of, inter alia, possession of a controlled substance and sentenced in May 2001, appellant's counsel failed to file post-sentence motions. Appellant's appeal from the judgment of sentence was quashed as untimely in May 2003 as Pa. R. Crim. P. 720(A)(1) only permitted a written post-sentence motion to toll the time period for the filing of a notice of appeal. In February 2004, appellant filed a petition under the Post Conviction Relief Act (PCRA), 42 Pa.C.S. §§ 9541-9546; relief on the merits was denied. The lower court quashed the appeal from that decision, citing a lack of jurisdiction based on the timing requirements of 42 Pa.C.S. § 9545(b). On further appeal, the court affirmed. The plain language of the PCRA in 42 Pa.C.S. § 9545(b)(3) allowed a postconviction petition to be filed within one year of the expiration of the time for seeking review; thus, the petition should have been filed in June 2002. Despite the alleged ineffectiveness of appellant's counsel, a statement in existing case law that the one-year period could commence 30 days after an appeal was quashed as untimely was dictum; no generalized equitable exception to the time bar existed.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the lower court's decision.

Commonwealth v. Gwynn


No. 398 CAP


SUPREME COURT OF PENNSYLVANIA


596 Pa. 398; 943 A.2d 940; 2008 Pa. LEXIS 259


March 29, 2005, Submitted 
March 20, 2008, Decided

Commonwealth v. Gwynn, 555 Pa. 86, 723 A.2d 143, 1998 Pa. LEXIS 2505 (1998)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the order of the Court of Common Pleas, Criminal Division of Philadelphia County (Pennsylvania), which denied his Post Conviction Relief Act (PCRA), 42 Pa.C.S. § 9541 et seq. petition for relief. Defendant was convicted by a jury of first degree murder and related charges. The court affirmed his conviction and sentence on direct appeal. The trial court (PCRA court) gave notice of its intention to dismiss the petition.


OVERVIEW: The PCRA court subsequently dismissed the petition without an evidentiary hearing, concluding each of the 16 issues raised by defendant were either previously litigated or meritless, pursuant to 42 Pa.C.S. §§ 9543(a)(3) and 9544(a)(2). The court noted that ineffective assistance of counsel claims were distinct from those claims raised on direct appeal and were to be treated as wholly independent of the underlying claim of error with regard to a PCRA petition. Ultimately, the court addressed each argument and found that they were either previously litigated or meritless.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the PCRA court's dismissal with regard to all of defendant's claims.

Commonwealth v. Romero


No. 315 CAP


SUPREME COURT OF PENNSYLVANIA


595 Pa. 275; 938 A.2d 362; 2007 Pa. LEXIS 2961


August 1, 2001, Submitted 
December 28, 2007, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Habeas corpus proceeding at, Motion granted by, in part, Motion denied by, in part Romero v. Beard, 2011 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 99009 (E.D. Pa., Aug. 31, 2011)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Appeal from the Ord of the CCP, Crim Div of Lehigh Cty entered on 09/15/2000 at No. 1827/1995 denying PCRA petition. Trial Court Judge: Thomas A. Wallitsch, J.
Commonwealth v. Romero, 555 Pa. 4, 722 A.2d 1014, 1999 Pa. LEXIS 37 (1999)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Lehigh County Court of Common Pleas, Criminal Division (Pennsylvania), entered a judgment that denied defendant's petition for relief pursuant to the Post Conviction Relief Act (PCRA), 42 Pa.C.S. § 9541 et seq. That denial came after a jury had found defendant guilty of first-degree murder, defendant had been sentenced to death, and that sentence had been affirmed on direct appeal. Defendant appealed the denial of his PCRA petition.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of the murder of a victim, a landlord, who was lured to a tenant's apartment under the pretense that the tenant intended to pay rent money. Defendant was eventually sentenced to death. After the sentence was affirmed on direct appeal, defendant's petition for post conviction relief was denied. The state supreme court found defendant could obtain post conviction relief if he could show that appellate counsel was ineffective for failing to pursue claims of trial counsel's ineffectiveness, which was known as a "layered claim." The state supreme court then found to preserve such a claim, the three-part Pierce test had to be met. It found that defendant adequately pled appellate counsel's ineffectiveness for not raising trial counsel's ineffectiveness, but did not show appellate counsel had no reasonable basis for pursuing the claim of trial counsel's ineffectiveness and that but for appellate counsel's ineffectiveness, the direct appeal result would have been different. The state supreme court then found that since all of defendant's underlying claims of trial counsel's ineffectiveness failed, his claims of appellate counsel's ineffectiveness failed as well.


OUTCOME: The state supreme court affirmed the trial court's judgment.

Commonwealth v. Copenhefer


No. 375 CAP


SUPREME COURT OF PENNSYLVANIA


596 Pa. 104; 941 A.2d 646; 2007 Pa. LEXIS 2930


January 24, 2006, Submitted 
December 28, 2007, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Writ of habeas corpus granted, in part, Writ of habeas corpus denied, in part Copenhefer v. Horn, 2012 U.S. App. LEXIS 20265 (3d Cir. Pa., Sept. 27, 2012)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Appeal from the Order entered on 4-8-2002 in the Court of Common Pleas, Criminal Division of Erie County denying the PCRA relief at No. 1325 A & B 1988. Trial Court Judge: Fred P. Anthony.
Commonwealth v. Copenhefer, 553 Pa. 285, 719 A.2d 242, 1998 Pa. LEXIS 2147 (1998)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant inmate, who had been sentenced to death, filed a petition against appellee Commonwealth of Pennsylvania under the Post Conviction Relief Act (PCRA), 42 Pa.C.S. §§ 9541 - 9546. The Court of Common Pleas, Criminal Division of Erie County (Pennsylvania) denied the petition as untimely under 42 Pa.C.S. § 9545. The inmate appealed.


OVERVIEW: The inmate based his petition on the court's decision in Rizzuto, which held that where a mitigating circumstance was presented to a jury by stipulation, the jury was required to find that mitigating factor. The inmate argued that the time-bar exception in § 9545(b)(1)(iii) applied because he had filed his petition within 60 days after Rizzuto was decided. The PCRA court dismissed the petition on the ground that because Rizzuto neither recognized a new constitutional right nor directed that its holding should be applied retroactively, § 9545(b)(1)(iii) did not apply. The court agreed. Although Rizzuto created a new rule of law, the court had not held that new rule to be constitutional in nature, and clearly that ruling was based on interpretation of 42 Pa.C.S. § 9711. Furthermore, the court had not held that Rizzuto applied retroactively. The inmate's direct appeal was exhausted 30 days after it was decided on March 18, 1991, the time within which he could have filed a certiorari petition, and thus was not pending when Rizzuto was decided in 2001. Thus, he was not entitled to retroactive application of Rizzuto.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the PCRA court's order.

Commonwealth v. Gordon


No. 46 EAP 2006


SUPREME COURT OF PENNSYLVANIA


596 Pa. 231; 942 A.2d 174; 2007 Pa. LEXIS 2938


April 16, 2007, Argued 
December 28, 2007, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: US Supreme Court certiorari denied by Gordon v. Pa., 128 S. Ct. 2094, 170 L. Ed. 2d 826, 2008 U.S. LEXIS 3810 (U.S., Apr. 28, 2008)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Appeal from the Judgment of Superior Court entered on April 20, 2006 at No. 1362 EDA 2004 Affirming in part and vacating in part the Judgment of Sentence entered on April 26, 2004 in the Court of Common Pleas, Philadelphia County, Criminal Division at No. CP-51-CR-0414381-2002. Appeal allowed: November 8, 2006 at 224 EAL 2006. Trial Court Judge: Eugene Edward J. Maier, Judge. Intermediate Court Judges: Debra Todd, John T. Kelly, JJ. Stephen J. McEwen, Jr., President Judge Emeritus.
Commonwealth v. Gordon, 902 A.2d 976, 2006 Pa. Super. LEXIS 2723 (Pa. Super. Ct., 2006)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Superior Court (Pennsylvania) entered an order that found the question of whether separated crimes constituted separate criminal transactions for the purpose of sentencing under the three-strikes sentencing provision of 42 Pa.C.S. § 9714(a)(2) was one of law and fell within the province of the court. Defendant petitioned to appeal his claim that 42 Pa.C.S. § 9714 was unconstitutional and the state supreme court granted limited review.


OVERVIEW: Following a trial, defendant was convicted of, inter alia, kidnapping. At the sentencing hearing, the parties stipulated that official court records would reveal his two prior first-degree felony convictions of robbery. Also, the Commonwealth provided certified court records indicating defendant had been sentenced to 25 to 50 years in prison for yet another first-degree felony robbery conviction. The trial court then sentenced defendant to life in prison upon conviction of kidnapping pursuant to the mandatory sentencing provision of 42 Pa.C.S. § 9714. That provision allowed the trial court to determine, by a preponderance of the evidence, the previous convictions of the offender. Defendant unsuccessfully argued on appeal that 42 Pa.C.S. § 9714 was unconstitutional. The state supreme court found that a trial court could determine whether separate crimes involved separate criminal transactions for three strikes sentencing under 42 Pa.C.S. § 9714 since that inquiry involved an examination of official court records and was similar to a trial court being allowed under Apprendi to determine the fact of prior convictions in order to enhance sentencing beyond the statutory maximum.


OUTCOME: The state supreme court affirmed the appellate court's order.

Beyers v. Richmond


No. 38 EAP 2006


SUPREME COURT OF PENNSYLVANIA


594 Pa. 654; 937 A.2d 1082; 2007 Pa. LEXIS 2937


April 16, 2007, Argued 
December 28, 2007, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Motion granted by Beyers v. Richmond, 2008 Phila. Ct. Com. Pl. LEXIS 313 (2008)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Appeal from the Judgment of Superior Court entered on June 27, 2005, (reargument/reconsideration denied August 26, 2005) at No. 1162 EDA 2004, affirming the Judgment entered on May 19, 2004 in the Court of Common Pleas, Philadelphia County, Civil Division at No. 3278 January Term, 2002. Appeal allowed: August 21, 2006 at 552 EAL 2005. Trial Court Judge: Mark I. Bernstein, Judge. Intermediate Court Judges: Joan Orie Melvin, Richard B. Klein, Jack A. Panella, JJ.
Beyers v. Richmond (Appeal of Forceno), 883 A.2d 684, 2005 Pa. Super. LEXIS 2239 (Pa. Super. Ct., 2005)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellee client was awarded treble damages on her Pennsylvania Unfair Trade Practices and Consumer Protection Law (UTPCPL), 73 Pa.C.S. § 201-1 et seq., claim arising out of her attorney's conversion of settlement proceeds and appellant law firm's liability for the attorney's conduct. Post-trial motions were denied, and judgment was entered. The Pennsylvania Superior Court (intermediate court) affirmed. The firm appealed.


OVERVIEW: The state's highest court held that the UTPCPL did not apply to an attorney's conduct in collecting and distributing settlement proceeds. Application of the UTPCPL to such conduct would violate the separation of powers doctrine and would encroach upon the state's highest court's exclusive power under Pa. Const. art. V, § 10(c) to regulate the practice of law in Pennsylvania. The Pennsylvania General Assembly had no authority under the Pennsylvania Constitution to regulate the conduct of lawyers in the practice of law. Any application of the UTPCPL to the collection and distribution of settlement proceeds would purport to regulate the conduct of attorneys. The Pennsylvania Rules of Professional Conduct and Pennsylvania Rules of Disciplinary Enforcement exclusively addressed the conduct complained of, specifically Pa. R. Prof. Conduct 1.5(c), 1.15(b), 8.4(b), and 8.4(c) and Pa.R.D.E. 514. These rules provided the exclusive remedy for the complained of attorney misconduct. Although the firm's and the attorney's conduct was extremely disturbing, the damages award could not stand.


OUTCOME: The intermediate court's order was reversed. Jurisdiction was relinquished.

 

195 of 2746 DOCUMENTS


Phila. Entm't & Dev. v. City of Philadelphia


No. 143 EM 2007


SUPREME COURT OF PENNSYLVANIA


595 Pa. 538; 939 A.2d 290; 2007 Pa. LEXIS 2867


October 16, 2007, Submitted 
December 27, 2007, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY: Phila. Entm't & Dev. Ptnrs., L.P. v. City of Philadelphia, 594 Pa. 468, 937 A.2d 385, 2007 Pa. LEXIS 2407 (Pa., 2007)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner applicant filed an action for review under the Pennsylvania Race Horse Development and Gaming Act, 4 Pa.C.S. § 1101 et seq., against respondents, the City of Philadelphia and its Department of Licenses and Inspections, after the Department denied its application for a permit to construct an amusement arcade. Respondents argued that the court lacked jurisdiction under 4 Pa.C.S. § 1506 to consider the petition.


OVERVIEW: The court stated that § 1506 expressly provided that only those orders or determinations or decisions that were "final" were appealable. The Gaming Act did not define "final." The court held that a final decision was an order, decision, or determination on a zoning issue involving a licensed facility that was conclusive and appealable under a political subdivision's zoning provisions. This construction of § 1506 was consistent with and advanced the General Assembly's intent in the Gaming Act to preserve a political subdivision's authority to zone and subject the development of licensed facilities to local zoning regulations. The Notice of Refusal of the permit application here was not conclusive and appealable under the City's zoning ordinances. This was because the Philadelphia Code provided for yet another step in the permit application process, a review by and decision from the Zoning Hearing Board on the Department's denial of the permit. Accordingly, the court did not have jurisdiction over the applicant's petition.


OUTCOME: The court quashed the appeal.

 

196 of 2746 DOCUMENTS


Middletown Twp. v. Lands of Stone


No. 64 MAP 2006


SUPREME COURT OF PENNSYLVANIA


595 Pa. 607; 939 A.2d 331; 2007 Pa. LEXIS 2891


October 17, 2006, Argued 
December 27, 2007, Decided 
December 28, 2007, Judgment Entered


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Appeal from the Order of the Commonwealth Court entered September 15, 2005, at No. 2152 CD 2004, which Affirmed the Bucks County Court of Common Pleas Order entered September 28, 2004, at Nos. 2000-6119-25-6 and TPM22-005-007. Appeal allowed: April 28, 2006 at 877 MAL 2005. Trial Court Judge: Rea Behney Boylan, Judge. Intermediate Court Judges: James Gardner Colins, President Judge, Bernard L. McGinley, Robert E. Simpson, JJ. 882 A.2d 1066 (Pa. Cmwlth. 2005).
Middletown Twp. v. Lands of Stone, 882 A.2d 1066, 2005 Pa. Commw. LEXIS 519 (Pa. Commw. Ct., 2005)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The objections filed by an administrator of a decedent's estate to a second-class township's taking of a farm were overruled. The Pennsylvania Commonwealth Court (intermediate court) affirmed. The owner was granted a limited review as to whether the ruling was in error, and whether the Pennsylvania Open Space Lands Act (Lands Act), 32 Pa. Stat. Ann. § 5008, imposed any limitations on the exercise of eminent domain by second-class townships.


OVERVIEW: The state's highest court held that the township had the authority to condemn property under the Pennsylvania Second-Class Township Code, 23 Pa. Stat. Ann. § 67201, for any legitimate recreational purpose, even though the Lands Act did not extend the authority to the township to take for open space purposes. However, the true purpose in taking the farm was not recreation. The township's open space plan discussed the farm in terms of its agricultural and open space value. The options considered by the township for the farm did not support the taking. Under the Fifth Amendment, the owner could not be allowed to continue to farm the land as a condemnation had to serve a public purpose. The taking of 175 acres to allow the township to create a second entrance to a neighboring park if the township decided that in the future it would like to reinstitute a town celebration there was excessive. The township had not created a plan for the use of the farm for passive recreation purposes. The township wanted to acquire the farm to preserve it as open space in order to prevent its development. The taking was outside the township's authority.


OUTCOME: The intermediate court's order was reversed. The matter was remanded to the trial court for further proceedings consistent with the opinion. Jurisdiction was relinquished.

Commonwealth v. Natividad


No. 497 CAP


SUPREME COURT OF PENNSYLVANIA


595 Pa. 188; 938 A.2d 310; 2007 Pa. LEXIS 2897


September 5, 2007, Submitted 
December 27, 2007, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Appeal from the Order entered on 11-28-05 in the Court of Common Pleas, Criminal Division of Philadelphia County denying PCRA petition at Nos. 9704-0013 & 9707-312 July Term 1997. Trial Court Judge: David Savitt, Senior Judge.
Commonwealth v. Natividad, 565 Pa. 348, 773 A.2d 167, 2001 Pa. LEXIS 1296 (2001)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In a capital case, appellant challenged order of the Philadelphia County Court of Common Pleas (Pennsylvania), which denied his petition for relief filed pursuant to the Post Conviction Relief Act (PCRA), 42 Pa.C.S. §§ 9541-46.


OVERVIEW: All of appellant's claims alleged ineffective assistance of trial counsel. The supreme court found that appellant failed to develop the requisite prejudice at the guilt-phase of his capital murder trial by counsel's failure to investigate the licensing status of the victim's firearm, and thus failed to prove that trial counsel was ineffective pursuant to 42 Pa.C.S. § 9546(d) of the PCRA. Appellant's mere assertion that the victim's possession of an unlicensed firearm established criminal conduct on the victim's part would not only fall far short of the standards for a permissive inference, but would have almost no probative value to appellant's self-defense claim. Appellant's claim that counsel's failure to provide his psychologist with various records in a timely fashion prevented the psychologist from testifying effectively to certain mitigating factors was unsupported. While the psychologist noted that the information would have provided outside confirmation of appellant's drug-use history and further details of it, the psychologist did not state that the evidence would have changed the diagnosis he expressed in a report or to the jury.


OUTCOME: The order was affirmed. The Prothonotary was directed to transmit the complete record of the case to the Governor, pursuant to 42 Pa.C.S. § 9711(i).

In re Condemnation Proceeding by the Redevelopment Auth. of Phila. (1839 N. Eighth St.)


No. 36 EAP 2006


SUPREME COURT OF PENNSYLVANIA


595 Pa. 241; 938 A.2d 341; 2007 Pa. LEXIS 2894


April 16, 2007, Argued 
December 27, 2007, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Appeal from the Opinion and Order of the Commonwealth Court dated February 6, 2006 at No. 150 CD 2005. Reversing the Order of the Court of Common Pleas of Philadelphia County, Civil Division, dated January 4, 2005 at No. 2988 Nov. T. 2003. Appeal allowed: July 27, 2006 at 109 EAL 2006. Trial Court Judge: Matthew D. Carrafiello, Judge. Intermediate Court Judges: Bonnie Brigance Leadbetter, President Judge, James Gardner Colins, Doris A. Smith-Ribner, Dan Pellegrini, Renee Cohn Jubelirer, Robert E. Simpson, M. Hannah Leavitt, JJ.
A Condemnation Proceeding, 891 A.2d 820, 2006 Pa. Commw. LEXIS 31 (Pa. Commw. Ct., 2006)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The trial court found the taking of appellee condemnee's property due to its blighted condition was legitimate, and it refused to entertain any argument regarding whether the subsequent transfer of the property to a developer that was a religious entity violated the Establishment Clause. The Commonwealth Court (Pennsylvania) reversed. Appellant redevelopment authority petitioned the court for a grant of allocatur, which was granted.


OVERVIEW: The record did not support a bad faith claim against the redevelopment authority. Therefore, what remained was a review of whether the taking of the property violated the Establishment Clause. The secular purpose in the redevelopment authority's taking of the property was but another in a series of steps taken to eliminate blight, as established in the Urban Redevelopment Act. The elimination of blight was a valid public purpose that, in the absence of bad faith, was completely separate from any religious use of the property subsequent to the taking. The principal or primary effect of the taking was to eliminate blight in the neighborhood. While the religious nature of the school to be built on the property was reason for the court's careful review, the facts indicated no goal aside from the elimination of blight and did not provide any indication that the principal or primary effect would be to advance religion. The exercise of eminent domain to eliminate blight was a valid public purpose, and the subsequent sale of the property to a religious entity did not constitute "entanglement" that made the taking unconstitutional.


OUTCOME: To the extent that the commonwealth court found it necessary to overrule what it believed to be the trial court's finding of waiver for the condemnee's failure to challenge the certification of blight, the court affirmed. In all other respects, the court reversed and remanded to the commonwealth court for a determination of any outstanding issues consistent with the opinion.

Stilp v. Gen. Assembly


No. 76 MAP 2006, No. 80 MAP 2006


SUPREME COURT OF PENNSYLVANIA


596 Pa. 62; 940 A.2d 1227; 2007 Pa. LEXIS 2958


March 26, 2007, Submitted 
December 27, 2007, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
76 MAP 2006

Appeal from the Order of the Commonwealth Court, entered on April 24, 2006, at No. 513 MD 2005 Sustained the preliminary objection filed by respondents and petitioners petition for review is dismissed. Trial Court Judge: Dan Pellegrini, Commonwealth Court Judge. Intermediate Court Judges: Bonnie Brigance Leadbetter, President Judge, James Gardner Colins, Bernard L. McGinley, Dan Pellegrini, Rochelle S. Friedman, Robert E. Simpson, JJ.

80 MAP 2006

Appeal from the Order of the Commonwealth Court, entered on April 24, 2006, at No. 513 MD 2005 Dismissing Petitioner's petition for review. Trial Court Judge: Dan Pellegrini, Commonwealth Court Judge. Intermediate Court Judges: Bonnie Brigance Leadbetter, President Judge, James Gardner Colins, Bernard L. McGinley, Dan Pellegrini, Rochelle S. Friedman, Robert E. Simpson, JJ.

898 A.2d 36 (Pa. Cmwlth. 2006).
Stilp v. Commonwealth, 898 A.2d 36, 2006 Pa. Commw. LEXIS 201 (Pa. Commw. Ct., 2006)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Commonwealth Court (Pennsylvania) entered a judgment that determined petitioner taxpayer had standing to bring a declaratory judgment action regarding an audit of the General Assembly's financial accounts, but which concluded that no constitutional or statutory authority existed that the Auditor General had the power to audit those accounts. The taxpayer appealed and respondent senators cross-appealed the standing ruling.


OVERVIEW: The taxpayer petitioned for review in the Commonwealth Court seeking a declaratory judgment that the Auditor General had the authority to audit the General Assembly's financial accounts. The senators responded by claiming, inter alia, that the taxpayer lacked standing to bring such an action. The Commonwealth Court initially determined that the taxpayer possessed the requirements for taxpayer standing. It ultimately concluded, however, that the taxpayer failed to provide either constitutional or statutory authority supporting the position that the Auditor General can, and must, audit the General Assembly. The taxpayer appealed the ruling against him. The senators cross-appealed the standing determination. The state supreme court found that it was not necessary to consider the Auditor General's authority because the taxpayer lacked standing to bring the action. The state supreme court applied the five-factor Biester taxpayer standing test and concluded that the taxpayer did not meet the fifth factor, that no other persons were better suited to assert the claim, because the Auditor General could in his discretion file such a declaratory judgment action.


OUTCOME: The state supreme court affirmed the appellate court's judgment.

Oz Gas, Ltd. v. Warren Area Sch. Dist.


Nos. 10, 11, 12 WAP 2006


SUPREME COURT OF PENNSYLVANIA


595 Pa. 128; 938 A.2d 274; 2007 Pa. LEXIS 2882; 167 Oil & Gas Rep. 791


March 5, 2007, Argued 
December 27, 2007, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: US Supreme Court certiorari denied by Oz Gas v. Warren Area Sch. Dist., 128 S. Ct. 2508, 171 L. Ed. 2d 788, 2008 U.S. LEXIS 4431 (U.S., May 27, 2008)


PRIOR HISTORY: 10 WAP 2006 [***1] 
Appeals from the Order of the Commonwealth Court entered November 9, 2005, at No. 1550 CD 2004, reversing the Order of the Court of Common Pleas of Warren County entered July 2, 2004, at A.D. 242 of 2003. Appeal allowed June 14, 2006 at 639 WAL 2005. Trial Court Judge: William F. Morgan, President Judge. Intermediate Court Judges: James Gardner Colins, Bernard L. McGinley, Dan Pellegrini, Rochelle S. Friedman, Renee Jubelirer Cohn, Robert E. Simpson, Hannah M. Leavitt, JJ. 886 A.2d 336 (Pa. Cmwlth. 2005).
11 WAP 2006
Appeals from the Order of the Commonwealth Court entered November 9, 2005, at No. 1550 CD 2004, reversing the Order of the Court of Common Pleas of Warren County entered July 2, 2004, at A.D. 242 of 2003. Appeal allowed June 14, 2006 at 654 WAL 2005. Trial Court Judge: William F. Morgan, President Judge. Intermediate Court Judges: James Gardner Colins, Bernard L. McGinley, Dan Pellegrini, Rochelle S. Friedman, Renee Jubelirer Cohn, Robert E. Simpson, Hannah M. Leavitt, JJ.
12 WAP 2006
Appeals from the Order of the Commonwealth Court entered November 9, 2005, at No. 1550 CD 2004, reversing the Order of the Court of Common Pleas of Warren County entered July 2, 2004, at A.D. 242 of 2003. Appeal allowed June 14, 2006 at 660 WAL 2005. Trial Court Judge: William F. Morgan, President Judge. Intermediate Court Judges: James Gardner Colins, Bernard L. McGinley, Dan Pellegrini, Rochelle S. Friedman, Renee Jubelirer Cohn, Robert E. Simpson, Hannah M. Leavitt, JJ.
Oz Gas, Ltd. v. Warren Area Sch. Dist., 886 A.2d 336, 2005 Pa. Commw. LEXIS 686 (Pa. Commw. Ct., 2005)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellee taxpayer filed an action against appellant taxing authorities in which the taxpayer sought a refund under 72 Pa. Stat. Ann. § 5566b of ad valorem taxes it had paid on oil and gas reserves that remained in the ground. The trial court granted the taxing authorities' motion for summary judgment. The Commonwealth Court (Pennsylvania) reversed. The taxing authorities appealed.


OVERVIEW: In 2002, the present court held that 72 Pa. Stat. Ann. § 5020-201(a) precluded counties from collecting taxes on oil and gas reserves that remained in the ground. The taxpayer argued that the decision should apply retroactively. The court noted that it had previously held that a decision striking down a state tax on constitutional grounds applied prospectively only. Accordingly, the 2002 holding, based on statutory interpretation, should also apply prospectively. This holding was buttressed by application of the Chevron test. The 2002 decision established a new principle of law, and applying it retroactively would not forward the operation of the decision. The equities weighed heavily in favor of prospective-only application, as the taxing authorities had collected and used the taxes with the good faith belief that they were legally entitled to them. Requiring a refund would cause substantial financial hardship to the communities involved. Because the 2002 decision had prospective application only, the taxing authorities were entitled to the taxes prior to that decision, and no refund was warranted under 72 Pa. Stat. Ann. § 5566b.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the decision of the Commonwealth Court.
